السبب في حدوث الظاهرة، أو هو يشتمل على السبب الحقيقي.
وفي مجال التجربة العملية لاكتشاف سبب وباء انتشر في حظائر تربية الدجاج، فرض الباحث أن السبب يرجع إلى عنصر خاص من عناصر غذائها.
ولتحقيق صحة هذا الفرض أو ترجيحه، وضع الباحث عدة مجموعات سليمة، وأخذ من أنواع الأغذية التي تتناولها ذات الوباء المنتشر، ثم قدم لكل مجموعتين منعزلتين مركباً معيناً من مجموعة عناصر الغذاء الذي يقدم لذات الوباء، ثم وجد بعد إجراء التجربة أن الوباء ظهر في بعض المجموعات التي يحتوي غذاؤها على مادة خاصة.
عندئذ يتأكد الباحث من صحة الفرض الذي فرضه، ويجزم بأن هذا العنصر الغذائي هو سبب الوباء.
قيمة هذه الطريقة :
وعلى الرغم من شيوع هذه الطريقة وكثرة استعمالها، إلا أنها لا تفيد يقيناً علمياً، وإنما تفيد رجحاناً ظنياً فقط، لاحتمال تعدد الأسباب للظواهر المتماثلة، فالموت ظاهرة قد تحدث بسبب مرض في القلب، أو مرض في الرئتين، أو مرض في الكبد، أو بسبب انفجار في المخ، أو بسبب ارتفاع نسبة البولة في الدم، أو غير ذلك من أسباب لا تحصى، فهل لنا أن نأخذ مجموعة ـ مهما كانت كبيرة ـ من الذين أصابتهم الوفاة، ونجري عملية الاستقراء عليهم، فإذا تبين لنا أنهم اشتركوا في تضخم الكبد واختلفوا فيما عدا ذلك، حكمنا بأن تضخم الكبد كان هو سبب وفاتهم، مع أننا لاحظنا أن بعضهم عنده انفجار في المخ أيضاً، وبعضهم مريض بالقلب، وبعضهم مصاب بالسل، وهكذا؟ ألا يحتمل أن كل واحد منهم كانت وفاته بسبب من هذه الأسباب الكثيرة، مع اشتراك الجميع بسبب واحد، وظاهرة الموت واحدة في الجميع؟ وهنا يحسن أن نذكر قول الشاعر:
ومن لم يمت بالسيف مات بغيره تنوعت الأسباب والموت واحد
وقد انتقدت هذه الطريقة بأنها صعبة التطبيق، إذ لا تكاد تتفق حالتان أو أكثر لظاهرة من الظواهر في ظرف واحد، مع الاختلاف في جميع الظروف الأخرى، إذ الطبيعة العامة معقدة، فهي تحتوي على كثير من الأسباب والمسببات المتشابكة المتداخلة، وبذلك تشتبه الأمور، ويكون من الصعب جداً فصل ظرف خاص عن بقية الظروف الأخرى.
وانتقدت باحتمال كون اتفاق الحالتين للظاهرة في ظرف واحد فقط واختلافهما فيما عداه، إنما كان من قبيل المصادفة المحضة، دون أن يكون هذا الظرف الواحد هو السبب للظاهرة أو مشتملاً على السبب، وهذا الانتقاد يؤيد أن هذه الطريقة لا تفيد يقيناً، وإنما تفيد رجحاناً ظنياً فقط.
The cause of the occurrence of the phenomenon, or it includes the real cause. In the field of practical experiment to discover the cause of an epidemic that spread in chicken farms, the researcher hypothesized that the cause is due to a specific element of their feed. To verify or support this hypothesis, the researcher set up several healthy groups, took from the types of feed that the epidemic-stricken chickens consume, then presented to each isolated pair a specific compound from the set of feed elements given to the epidemic-stricken ones. Then after conducting the experiment, he found that the epidemic appeared in some groups whose feed contained a particular substance. At that point, the researcher becomes certain of the validity of his hypothesis and concludes that this food element is the cause of the epidemic. Value of this method: Despite the prevalence and frequent use of this method, it does not yield scientific certainty, but only probable preference, due to the possibility of multiple causes for similar phenomena. For death is a phenomenon that may occur due to heart disease, lung disease, liver disease, brain hemorrhage, elevated blood urea, or countless other causes. So can we take a group—no matter how large—of those who died, perform induction on them, and if it becomes clear to us that they all shared an enlarged liver and differed in everything else, we judge that enlarged liver was the cause of their death, even though we observed that some had brain hemorrhage, some had heart disease, some had tuberculosis, and so on? Is it not possible that each one of them died from one of these many causes, while all share one cause, and the phenomenon of death is the same in all? And here it is appropriate to mention the poet's saying: 'And whoever does not die by the sword dies by something else; the causes are varied but death is one.' This method has been criticized for being difficult to apply, since two or more cases of a phenomenon hardly ever agree in one circumstance while differing in all other circumstances, because nature is complex and contains many intertwined and overlapping causes and effects, thus matters become confused, and it is very difficult to isolate a particular circumstance from the rest. It has also been criticized by the possibility that the agreement of two cases of the phenomenon in only one circumstance and their difference in others is merely a coincidence, without that single circumstance being the cause of the phenomenon or containing the cause. And this criticism supports that this method does not yield certainty, but only probable preference.
Source pages p. 217

Commentary
This passage describes the experimental inductive method for discovering causes and critically evaluates its epistemological value. The author begins with an example: to find the cause of a chicken epidemic, a researcher hypothesizes that a specific feed element is responsible. He sets up several healthy groups and gives them different feed compounds. Observing that the epidemic appears only in groups receiving a particular substance, he concludes that substance is the cause. The author then assesses the method: despite its frequent use, it does not produce certainty (يقين), only probability (رجحان ظني). The reason is that multiple causes can produce the same effect. To illustrate, he lists many possible causes of death. If we observe a group of deceased people and find they all had enlarged livers but differed in other conditions, we cannot be sure enlarged liver caused death, because they may have died from other diseases present. The author supports this with a poetic couplet: 'Causes vary but death is one.' Two criticisms follow: first, the method is hard to apply because nature is complex, making it difficult to find cases that agree in only one circumstance; second, even if such cases are found, the agreement might be coincidental. Both criticisms reinforce that the method yields only probable knowledge, not certainty.

سبب
فرض

In the chicken epidemic example, what pattern causes the researcher to conclude that the specific food substance is the cause?

C) The substance was present in all cases of the epidemic and absent in all healthy cases.
D) The researcher observed the epidemic before the experiment.

Key Takeaway
The inductive method of agreement and difference can suggest causal relations but does not guarantee certainty due to the possibility of multiple or hidden causes.

Induction and Analogy

Why Induction Cannot Yield Certainty
Author critiques the inductive method's epistemological value

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to articulate the two main criticisms of the inductive method presented in the passage and explain why induction yields only probable knowledge.

Core Idea
Induction fails to produce certainty because multiple causes can produce the same effect.

After explaining the inductive method, the author turns to its epistemological limitations. In this lesson, you will analyze the two critical objections: the possibility of multiple causes and the difficulty of isolating variables. Understanding these limitations is crucial for correctly assessing the strength of inductive arguments in Islamic sciences.

Guided Path
1
Locate the author's central critique
Read the section starting from 'قيمة هذه الطريقة' and notice the shift: the author states that despite widespread use, the method does not yield certainty. Find the key phrase: 'لا تفيد يقيناً علمياً، وإنما تفيد رجحاناً ظنياً فقط'.
The author's main claim is that induction gives only probability (رجحان ظني), not certainty (يقين).
2
Understand the multiple-causes objection
The author uses the example of death to show that many different causes can produce the same phenomenon. Even if many cases share one factor (e.g., enlarged liver), each death may have a different actual cause. This undermines the inductive leap from correlation to causation.
The poetic line 'تنوعت الأسباب والموت واحد' encapsulates this idea.
3
Identify the practical difficulty objection
The second criticism is that it is nearly impossible to find two cases that agree in only one circumstance while differing in all others. Nature is too complex and intertwined, making isolation of a single variable extremely difficult.
This criticism targets the feasibility of the method itself.
4
Recognize the coincidence objection
Even if two cases appear to agree in one circumstance, the agreement might be coincidental. The shared factor might not be the cause at all. This reinforces that induction cannot provide certainty.
This is a logical possibility that prevents conclusive inference.

Source Text

Value of this method: Despite the prevalence and frequent use of this method, it does not yield scientific certainty, but only probable preference, due to the possibility of multiple causes for similar phenomena. For death is a phenomenon that may occur due to heart disease, lung disease, liver disease, brain hemorrhage, elevated blood urea, or countless other causes. So can we take a group—no matter how large—of those who died, perform induction on them, and if it becomes clear to us that they all shared an enlarged liver and differed in everything else, we judge that enlarged liver was the cause of their death, even though we observed that some had brain hemorrhage, some had heart disease, some had tuberculosis, and so on? Is it not possible that each one of them died from one of these many causes, while all share one cause, and the phenomenon of death is the same in all? And here it is appropriate to mention the poet's saying: 'And whoever does not die by the sword dies by something else; the causes are varied but death is one.' This method has been criticized for being difficult to apply, since two or more cases of a phenomenon hardly ever agree in one circumstance while differing in all other circumstances, because nature is complex and contains many intertwined and overlapping causes and effects, thus matters become confused, and it is very difficult to isolate a particular circumstance from the rest. It has also been criticized by the possibility that the agreement of two cases of the phenomenon in only one circumstance and their difference in others is merely a coincidence, without that single circumstance being the cause of the phenomenon or containing the cause. And this criticism supports that this method does not yield certainty, but only probable preference.
Source pages p. 217

Commentary
This passage describes the experimental inductive method for discovering causes and critically evaluates its epistemological value. The author begins with an example: to find the cause of a chicken epidemic, a researcher hypothesizes that a specific feed element is responsible. He sets up several healthy groups and gives them different feed compounds. Observing that the epidemic appears only in groups receiving a particular substance, he concludes that substance is the cause. The author then assesses the method: despite its frequent use, it does not produce certainty (يقين), only probability (رجحان ظني). The reason is that multiple causes can produce the same effect. To illustrate, he lists many possible causes of death. If we observe a group of deceased people and find they all had enlarged livers but differed in other conditions, we cannot be sure enlarged liver caused death, because they may have died from other diseases present. The author supports this with a poetic couplet: 'Causes vary but death is one.' Two criticisms follow: first, the method is hard to apply because nature is complex, making it difficult to find cases that agree in only one circumstance; second, even if such cases are found, the agreement might be coincidental. Both criticisms reinforce that the method yields only probable knowledge, not certainty.

سبب
فرض

Key Takeaway
The inductive method of agreement and difference is epistemologically limited: it provides probable knowledge, not certainty, due to the possibility of multiple causes and practical difficulties in isolating variables.

Inductive Extraction of the 'Illa of Riba
Author applies the inductive method to prophetic hadith to derive the 'illa of riba as being weighed items.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the inductive method to extract the 'illa of a legal ruling from prophetic hadith, as demonstrated in the case of riba.

Core Idea
Induction in fiqh yields a probable 'illa, not certainty, but it is essential for ta'lil.

In the previous lesson, you learned the logical critique of induction: it does not produce certainty. However, in Islamic jurisprudence, induction is a practical necessity for extracting the cause of rulings (ta'lil). This lesson walks you through the real application: how jurists used induction on the riba hadith to identify the 'illa of riba as being sold by weight, enabling juridical analogy.

Guided Path
1
Examine the hadith instances
Read the hadith listing six commodities: gold, silver, wheat, barley, dates, and salt. Note the ruling: same type must be equal and hand-to-hand; different types only hand-to-hand required.
The hadith is from Muslim and Abu Sa'id al-Khudri.
2
Search for a common attribute
Look for a property shared by all six items. The text says jurists found only one common attribute: they are all sold by weight (mawzuna). No other property (e.g., being food or precious metal) applies to all.
Consider why other attributes fail (e.g., dates are food, gold is not).
3
Propose the 'illa
Conclude that the common attribute (being weighed) is the 'illa (effective cause) for the prohibition of riba in these items. This is the inductive step: generalizing from the instances.
Induction here is incomplete (istiqra' naqis) – only six items, but jurists treat it as strong evidence.
4
Apply the 'illa via juridical analogy
Use the extracted 'illa to extend the ruling to any weighed item. If the item is weighed, riba is prohibited: same type requires equality and hand-to-hand; different types require only hand-to-hand.
This is al-qiyas al-usuli, not logical analogy.
5
Critically evaluate the induction
Recall the earlier critique: this induction is not complete (tamm) and yields only probability (zann). The 'illa is a juristic construct, not a necessary truth.
The author's point is not to dismiss usul al-fiqh but to show its epistemic status.

هذه الطريقة هي إحدى طرق استخراج علة الحكم في الفقه الإسلامي.
نظر الأصوليون في قول الرسول ﷺ الذي رواه مسلم عن عبادة بن الصامت: «الذهب بالذهب، والفضة بالفضة، والبر بالبر، والشعير بالشعير، والتمر بالتمر، والملح بالملح، مثلاً بمثل، سواءً بسواء، يداً بيد، فإذا اختلفت هذه الأصناف فبيعوا كيف شئتم إذا كان يداً بيد» وفي رواية أبي سعيد الخدري بعد «يداً بيد» أن الرسول قال: «فمن زاد أو استزاد فقد أربى، والآخذ والمعطي فيه سواء».
وقد بحث المجتهدون في علة تحريم الربا في هذه الأصناف، فنظر بعضهم إليها جميعاً، فلم يجد صفة مشتركة بينها جميعاً إلا كونها موزونة، فحكم بأن علة تحريم الربا فيها كونها موزونة، فرأى على طريق القياس الأصولي أن كل عنصر موزون يتبايع فيه الناس يحرم فيه الربا، فإن اتحد الصنف وجب فيه التساوي (سواء بسواء) دون زيادة، ووجبت فيه المقابضة (يداً بيد) دون تأجيل وإن اختلف الصنفان لم يشترط فيهما التساوي، وإنما اشترط فيهما المقابضة.
This method is one of the methods of extracting the cause of a ruling in Islamic jurisprudence. The usul scholars considered the saying of the Messenger ﷺ, narrated by Muslim from Ubadah ibn al-Samit: 'Gold for gold, silver for silver, wheat for wheat, barley for barley, dates for dates, salt for salt, like for like, equal for equal, hand to hand; if these types differ, then sell as you wish provided it is hand to hand.' And in the narration of Abu Sa'id al-Khudri after 'hand to hand', the Messenger said: 'Whoever increases or asks for increase has engaged in riba, the taker and the giver are alike therein.' The mujtahids researched the cause of the prohibition of riba in these items. Some of them looked at all of them together and found no common attribute among them except that they are weighed. So they ruled that the cause of the prohibition of riba in them is that they are weighed. Then, on the basis of juridical analogy, they held that any weighed item that people trade in is subject to the prohibition of riba. If the type is the same, then equality (like for like) without increase is obligatory, and hand-to-hand exchange is obligatory without deferment. If the two types differ, then equality is not required, but hand-to-hand exchange is required.
Source pages p. 218

Commentary
This passage illustrates the practical application of the previously criticized inductive method in Islamic jurisprudence (usul al-fiqh) to extract the 'illa (effective cause) of a legal ruling. The author explicitly states that the method described earlier is one of the tools used by jurists to find the cause of a ruling. The example is the prohibition of riba in the well-known hadith listing six commodities: gold, silver, wheat, barley, dates, and salt. The hadith stipulates that when these items are exchanged for the same type, they must be equal in quantity and exchanged hand to hand; if different types, only hand to hand is required. Jurists examined these six items to find a common attribute that could be the 'illa (cause) of the prohibition. They observed that the only common attribute among all six is that they are sold by weight (موزونة). Therefore, they concluded that being weighed is the 'illa. Using juridical analogy (قياس أصولي), they extended the ruling to any weighed item traded among people. They then derived the detailed rules: if the same type (e.g., gold for gold), equality and hand-to-hand are required; if different types (e.g., gold for silver), only hand-to-hand is required, not equality. This demonstrates how the inductive method (finding a common attribute among instances) is used in fiqh despite its epistemological limitations.

Key Takeaway
Induction in usul al-fiqh, though probable, is a practical tool for extracting the 'illa from scriptural instances, as demonstrated by the derivation of riba's 'illa as being weighed.

How would a different induction produce a different 'illa (e.g., being food)? Examine why the jurists chose 'mawzuna' over other possible attributes.

Induction and Analogy

The Method of Concordance (al-Tard) for Extracting the 'Illa
Author explains the method of concordance with the riba example.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the method of concordance to identify the 'illa in a set of analogous rulings from Islamic jurisprudence.

Core Idea
Concordance finds the common attribute among cases to extract the legal cause.

In Usul al-Fiqh, jurists need to identify the effective cause ('illa) behind a ruling to extend it to new cases via analogy. One method is concordance (tard): examining multiple cases that share the same ruling and extracting the attribute common to all. This lesson walks through the example of riba to show how concordance works.

Guided Path
1
Identify the cases sharing the same ruling
Look for multiple instances where the same legal ruling applies. In the riba example, gold and silver are one group; wheat, barley, dates, and salt are another group. All are subject to the prohibition of riba.
2
List the attributes of each case
For each case, list all possible attributes that could be relevant. For gold and silver, attributes include colour, value, currency, weight. For the food items, attributes include being food, being measurable, price.
3
Find the attribute common to all cases
Identify which attribute is present in every case but absent in others that are not subject to the ruling. For gold and silver, the common attribute is being currency or weight; for the food items, it is being food or being measurable.
The common attribute is the suspected 'illa.
4
Test the attribute's necessity and sufficiency
Check if the common attribute is indeed present whenever the ruling applies and absent when it does not. Jurists verified that currency and food are consistently linked to riba.
This step is probabilistic, not certain.
5
Apply the 'illa via qiyas
Once the 'illa is identified, extend the ruling to any new case sharing that attribute. For example, any food item is analogized to the original cases, making riba applicable.
This is a standard usuli analogy.

Source Text

ونظر بعضهم إليها فقسمها إلى قسمين : فجعل الذهب والفضة قسماً، واستخرج الصفة المشتركة بينهما، وحكم بأنها هي علة الربا فيهما، وهذه الصفة هي النقدية، أو الوزن. وجعل البر والشعير والتمر والملح قسماً ثانياً، واستخرج الصفة المشتركة بينها؛ وحكم بأنها هي علة الربا فيها، وهذه الصفة هي كونها مطعومة، فقاس عليها كل مطعوم قياساً أصولياً، أو كونها مكيلة فقاس عليها كل مكيل . وتدخل هذه الطريقة ضمن أنواع «تخريج مناط الحكم» المعروفة في علم أصول الفقه . واستخراج العلة بهذه الطريقة، استخراج لها عن طريق الطرد. ٢ - شرح الطريقة الثانية : وهي النظر في الاختلاف، أي النظر إلى حالات الظاهرة المدروسة، واستخراج الظرف الوحيد الذي تَخَلَّف وجود الظاهرة بتخلف وجوده، مع وجود الظروف الأخرى عند تخلف وجود الظاهرة . يقول «ستيوارت ميل» في تحديد هذه الطريقة : «إذا وجدت الظاهرة في حالة ولم توجد في حالة أخرى، وكانت الحالتان متفقتين في جميع الظروف إلا في ظرف واحد، يوجد عند وجود الظاهرة ولا يوجد عند اختفائها، كان هذا الظرف سبب الظاهرة» . ليس خافياً أن هذه الطريقة هي عكس الطريقة الأولى، فالطريقة الأولى تعتمد على اختلاف الحالات في كل الظروف، إلا في الظرف الذي تحدث فيه الظاهرة فهو متفق، وهذه الطريقة الثانية تعتمد على اتفاق الحالات في كل الظروف إلا في الظرف الذي تحدث فيه الظاهرة، فهو مختلف . مثال ذلك : مفرختان للدجاج متفقتان في كل ظروفهما إلا أن إحداهما معطاة نسبة ما من الرطوبة والأخرى جافة تماماً . أما الأولى فقد فقس بيضها وأعطت نتيجة حسنة، وأما الأخرى فقد كانت على عكس ذلك. هنا لا بد أن يتنبه الباحث إلى أن السبب في نجاح عمل الأولى، وجود النسبة المطلوبة من الرطوبة إضافة إلى الشروط الأخرى، وأن السبب في إخفاق عمل الثانية هو عدم وجود النسبة المطلوبة من الرطوبة، مع اتفاق ظروفها مع ظروف الأولى، من كل الوجوه إلا من هذا الوجه. ونمثل لها أيضاً بانطفاء عود الثقاب المشتعل إذا أدخل في إناء مفرغ من الهواء، واستمراره مشتعلاً إذا أدخل في إناء مليء بالهواء، وهنا نلاحظ أن الحالتين متفقتان في كل الظروف، إلا في ظرف واحد هو وجود الهواء عند ظاهرة الاشتعال، وعدم وجوده عند ظاهرة الانطفاء، وهذا يجعلنا نؤكد أن سبب الاشتعال هو وجود الهواء. قيمة هذه الطريقة : هذه الطريقة أيضاً لا تفيد يقيناً علمياً، وإنما تفيد رجحاناً ظنياً فقط، لاحتمال أن يكون الاختلاف في عدد من الأمور الجزئية، وأن يكون سبب الظاهرة في الحقيقة واحداً منها، والأجزاء الأخرى المرافقة متفقة التلازم لا تنفك . وهذه الطريقة لا تخلو من عيوب الطريقة الأولى، ولكنها على كل حال أفضل منها، وذلك لأنه من العسير جداً أن تختلف الحالتان في كل ظروفهما إلا في ظرف واحد، في حين أنه من السهل أن تتفق الحالتان في كل ظروفهما إلا في ظرف واحد. هذه الطريقة هي إحدى طرق استخراج علة الحكم في الفقه الإسلامي. نظر الأصوليون في علة تحريم الخمر، فسبروا الصفات التي تتصف بها هذه المادة، من سيولة، ولون، وكونها من أصل حلو، وغير ذلك، فوجدوا أن شيئاً منها لم تظهر له آثار حرمة في أي شراب آخر لا مفترقاً ولا مجتمعاً،
And some people looked at it and divided it into two sections: They made gold and silver one section, extracted the common attribute between them, and ruled that it is the cause of riba in them, and this attribute is currency or weight. And they made wheat, barley, dates, and salt a second section, extracted the common attribute between them, and ruled that it is the cause of riba in them, and this attribute is being food, so they analogized every food through it in an usuli analogy, or being measurable, so they analogized every measurable. And this method enters under the types of 'extracting the basis of the ruling' known in the science of Usul al-Fiqh. Extracting the cause by this method is extraction by way of concordance. 2. Explanation of the second method: It is looking at difference, i.e., looking at the states of the studied phenomenon, and extracting the single circumstance the absence of which accompanies the absence of the phenomenon, while other circumstances are present at the absence of the phenomenon. John Stuart Mill says in defining this method: 'If the phenomenon is found in one case and not found in another case, and the two cases are identical in all circumstances except one circumstance present when the phenomenon occurs and absent when it disappears, then this circumstance is the cause of the phenomenon.' It is not hidden that this method is the opposite of the first method: the first method relies on difference of cases in all circumstances except the circumstance in which the phenomenon occurs, which is common; and this second method relies on agreement of cases in all circumstances except the circumstance in which the phenomenon occurs, which is different. Example: two chicken incubators identical in all circumstances except that one is given a certain percentage of humidity and the other is completely dry. As for the first, its eggs hatched and gave a good result; as for the other, it was the opposite. Here the researcher must be aware that the reason for the success of the first is the presence of the required percentage of humidity in addition to the other conditions, and the reason for the failure of the second is the absence of the required percentage of humidity, while its conditions agree with the first in every aspect except this aspect. We also exemplify it with the extinguishing of a burning matchstick when inserted into a vacuum container, and its continuing to burn when inserted into an air-filled container. Here we observe that the two cases are identical in all circumstances except one circumstance: the presence of air during the phenomenon of ignition, and its absence during the phenomenon of extinguishment. This makes us confirm that the cause of ignition is the presence of air. Value of this method: This method also does not yield scientific certainty, but only probability, due to the possibility that the difference lies in a number of partial matters, and that the cause of the phenomenon in reality is one of them, while the other accompanying parts are consistently concomitant and inseparable. This method is not free from the defects of the first method, but it is nevertheless better than it, because it is very difficult for two cases to differ in all circumstances except one, while it is easy for two cases to agree in all circumstances except one. This method is one of the methods of extracting the cause of a ruling in Islamic jurisprudence. The usulis looked at the cause of the prohibition of wine: they explored the attributes that characterize this substance, such as fluidity, color, being derived from a sweet source, and others, and found that none of them showed effects of prohibition in any other drink, whether separately or collectively.
Source pages p. 219

Commentary
This passage explains two methods for extracting the 'illa (cause) of a ruling in Islamic jurisprudence, methods that are also used in inductive logic. The first method is the method of concordance (al-tard), where one looks for a common attribute among multiple cases of the same ruling. The author illustrates this with the example of riba (usury): scholars divided the ribawi items into two categories—gold and silver share the attribute of being currency or weight, while wheat, barley, dates, and salt share the attribute of being food or being measurable. They then extended the ruling to any item sharing that attribute via analogical reasoning (qiyas). This method is classified under 'extracting the basis of the ruling' (takhrij manat al-hukm) in Usul al-Fiqh. The second method is the method of difference (al-ikhtilaf), which looks for the unique circumstance that is present when the phenomenon occurs and absent when it does not, while all other circumstances remain the same. The author quotes John Stuart Mill's formulation of this method. Two examples are given: one from chicken incubators (humidity affects hatching) and one from a burning match (air is necessary for combustion). The passage then evaluates the methods: neither yields certainty, only probability, because multiple factors might be involved. However, the method of difference is considered better than the method of concordance because it is easier to find two cases that agree in all but one circumstance than to find two cases that differ in all but one. The passage concludes by tying this to Islamic jurisprudence, mentioning how usulis examined the attributes of wine and found none alone to be the cause of prohibition. The key lesson is that inductive methods are valuable but fallible tools for discovering causes.

طرد
تخريج مناط الحكم

Induction and Analogy

The Method of Difference (al-Ikhtilaf) for Extracting the 'Illa
Author explains the method of difference with examples and its application in fiqh.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the method of difference to isolate the 'illa by comparing two cases that agree in all respects except one.

Core Idea
Difference isolates the cause by comparing two cases that differ in only one circumstance.

The method of difference (ikhtilaf) is the second inductive method for extracting the 'illa. It compares two cases that are identical in all conditions except one: the suspected cause is present in one case and absent in the other, leading to different outcomes. This lesson explains the method and its application in Usul al-Fiqh, using examples from incubators and combustion, and discusses its probabilistic nature.

Guided Path
1
Identify two cases with different outcomes
Find one case where the phenomenon occurs and another where it does not. They should be as similar as possible. Example: a chicken incubator with humidity hatches eggs; one without humidity does not.
2
List all circumstances in both cases
Write down all relevant factors for each case. Ensure they are identical except for one circumstance. In the incubator example, all conditions are identical except humidity.
3
Identify the unique circumstance
The circumstance that differs between the two cases is the suspected cause. In the incubator, the presence of humidity in the successful case and its absence in the failure case point to humidity as the cause.
4
Apply the method to Islamic jurisprudence
Usulis apply this method to isolate the 'illa of a ruling. For example, in finding the cause of the prohibition of wine, they examine various substances that share many attributes but differ in the presence of the prohibition.
The passage mentions that usulis explored attributes of wine but found none alone to be the cause, suggesting the method can be challenging.
5
Evaluate the conclusion
Like concordance, this method yields only probability (zann) because the difference could involve multiple factors. However, it is considered more reliable than concordance because it is easier to find two cases that agree in all but one circumstance.

Source Text

ونظر بعضهم إليها فقسمها إلى قسمين : فجعل الذهب والفضة قسماً، واستخرج الصفة المشتركة بينهما، وحكم بأنها هي علة الربا فيهما، وهذه الصفة هي النقدية، أو الوزن. وجعل البر والشعير والتمر والملح قسماً ثانياً، واستخرج الصفة المشتركة بينها؛ وحكم بأنها هي علة الربا فيها، وهذه الصفة هي كونها مطعومة، فقاس عليها كل مطعوم قياساً أصولياً، أو كونها مكيلة فقاس عليها كل مكيل . وتدخل هذه الطريقة ضمن أنواع «تخريج مناط الحكم» المعروفة في علم أصول الفقه . واستخراج العلة بهذه الطريقة، استخراج لها عن طريق الطرد. ٢ - شرح الطريقة الثانية : وهي النظر في الاختلاف، أي النظر إلى حالات الظاهرة المدروسة، واستخراج الظرف الوحيد الذي تَخَلَّف وجود الظاهرة بتخلف وجوده، مع وجود الظروف الأخرى عند تخلف وجود الظاهرة . يقول «ستيوارت ميل» في تحديد هذه الطريقة : «إذا وجدت الظاهرة في حالة ولم توجد في حالة أخرى، وكانت الحالتان متفقتين في جميع الظروف إلا في ظرف واحد، يوجد عند وجود الظاهرة ولا يوجد عند اختفائها، كان هذا الظرف سبب الظاهرة» . ليس خافياً أن هذه الطريقة هي عكس الطريقة الأولى، فالطريقة الأولى تعتمد على اختلاف الحالات في كل الظروف، إلا في الظرف الذي تحدث فيه الظاهرة فهو متفق، وهذه الطريقة الثانية تعتمد على اتفاق الحالات في كل الظروف إلا في الظرف الذي تحدث فيه الظاهرة، فهو مختلف . مثال ذلك : مفرختان للدجاج متفقتان في كل ظروفهما إلا أن إحداهما معطاة نسبة ما من الرطوبة والأخرى جافة تماماً . أما الأولى فقد فقس بيضها وأعطت نتيجة حسنة، وأما الأخرى فقد كانت على عكس ذلك. هنا لا بد أن يتنبه الباحث إلى أن السبب في نجاح عمل الأولى، وجود النسبة المطلوبة من الرطوبة إضافة إلى الشروط الأخرى، وأن السبب في إخفاق عمل الثانية هو عدم وجود النسبة المطلوبة من الرطوبة، مع اتفاق ظروفها مع ظروف الأولى، من كل الوجوه إلا من هذا الوجه. ونمثل لها أيضاً بانطفاء عود الثقاب المشتعل إذا أدخل في إناء مفرغ من الهواء، واستمراره مشتعلاً إذا أدخل في إناء مليء بالهواء، وهنا نلاحظ أن الحالتين متفقتان في كل الظروف، إلا في ظرف واحد هو وجود الهواء عند ظاهرة الاشتعال، وعدم وجوده عند ظاهرة الانطفاء، وهذا يجعلنا نؤكد أن سبب الاشتعال هو وجود الهواء. قيمة هذه الطريقة : هذه الطريقة أيضاً لا تفيد يقيناً علمياً، وإنما تفيد رجحاناً ظنياً فقط، لاحتمال أن يكون الاختلاف في عدد من الأمور الجزئية، وأن يكون سبب الظاهرة في الحقيقة واحداً منها، والأجزاء الأخرى المرافقة متفقة التلازم لا تنفك . وهذه الطريقة لا تخلو من عيوب الطريقة الأولى، ولكنها على كل حال أفضل منها، وذلك لأنه من العسير جداً أن تختلف الحالتان في كل ظروفهما إلا في ظرف واحد، في حين أنه من السهل أن تتفق الحالتان في كل ظروفهما إلا في ظرف واحد. هذه الطريقة هي إحدى طرق استخراج علة الحكم في الفقه الإسلامي. نظر الأصوليون في علة تحريم الخمر، فسبروا الصفات التي تتصف بها هذه المادة، من سيولة، ولون، وكونها من أصل حلو، وغير ذلك، فوجدوا أن شيئاً منها لم تظهر له آثار حرمة في أي شراب آخر لا مفترقاً ولا مجتمعاً،
And some people looked at it and divided it into two sections: They made gold and silver one section, extracted the common attribute between them, and ruled that it is the cause of riba in them, and this attribute is currency or weight. And they made wheat, barley, dates, and salt a second section, extracted the common attribute between them, and ruled that it is the cause of riba in them, and this attribute is being food, so they analogized every food through it in an usuli analogy, or being measurable, so they analogized every measurable. And this method enters under the types of 'extracting the basis of the ruling' known in the science of Usul al-Fiqh. Extracting the cause by this method is extraction by way of concordance. 2. Explanation of the second method: It is looking at difference, i.e., looking at the states of the studied phenomenon, and extracting the single circumstance the absence of which accompanies the absence of the phenomenon, while other circumstances are present at the absence of the phenomenon. John Stuart Mill says in defining this method: 'If the phenomenon is found in one case and not found in another case, and the two cases are identical in all circumstances except one circumstance present when the phenomenon occurs and absent when it disappears, then this circumstance is the cause of the phenomenon.' It is not hidden that this method is the opposite of the first method: the first method relies on difference of cases in all circumstances except the circumstance in which the phenomenon occurs, which is common; and this second method relies on agreement of cases in all circumstances except the circumstance in which the phenomenon occurs, which is different. Example: two chicken incubators identical in all circumstances except that one is given a certain percentage of humidity and the other is completely dry. As for the first, its eggs hatched and gave a good result; as for the other, it was the opposite. Here the researcher must be aware that the reason for the success of the first is the presence of the required percentage of humidity in addition to the other conditions, and the reason for the failure of the second is the absence of the required percentage of humidity, while its conditions agree with the first in every aspect except this aspect. We also exemplify it with the extinguishing of a burning matchstick when inserted into a vacuum container, and its continuing to burn when inserted into an air-filled container. Here we observe that the two cases are identical in all circumstances except one circumstance: the presence of air during the phenomenon of ignition, and its absence during the phenomenon of extinguishment. This makes us confirm that the cause of ignition is the presence of air. Value of this method: This method also does not yield scientific certainty, but only probability, due to the possibility that the difference lies in a number of partial matters, and that the cause of the phenomenon in reality is one of them, while the other accompanying parts are consistently concomitant and inseparable. This method is not free from the defects of the first method, but it is nevertheless better than it, because it is very difficult for two cases to differ in all circumstances except one, while it is easy for two cases to agree in all circumstances except one. This method is one of the methods of extracting the cause of a ruling in Islamic jurisprudence. The usulis looked at the cause of the prohibition of wine: they explored the attributes that characterize this substance, such as fluidity, color, being derived from a sweet source, and others, and found that none of them showed effects of prohibition in any other drink, whether separately or collectively.
Source pages p. 219

Commentary
This passage explains two methods for extracting the 'illa (cause) of a ruling in Islamic jurisprudence, methods that are also used in inductive logic. The first method is the method of concordance (al-tard), where one looks for a common attribute among multiple cases of the same ruling. The author illustrates this with the example of riba (usury): scholars divided the ribawi items into two categories—gold and silver share the attribute of being currency or weight, while wheat, barley, dates, and salt share the attribute of being food or being measurable. They then extended the ruling to any item sharing that attribute via analogical reasoning (qiyas). This method is classified under 'extracting the basis of the ruling' (takhrij manat al-hukm) in Usul al-Fiqh. The second method is the method of difference (al-ikhtilaf), which looks for the unique circumstance that is present when the phenomenon occurs and absent when it does not, while all other circumstances remain the same. The author quotes John Stuart Mill's formulation of this method. Two examples are given: one from chicken incubators (humidity affects hatching) and one from a burning match (air is necessary for combustion). The passage then evaluates the methods: neither yields certainty, only probability, because multiple factors might be involved. However, the method of difference is considered better than the method of concordance because it is easier to find two cases that agree in all but one circumstance than to find two cases that differ in all but one. The passage concludes by tying this to Islamic jurisprudence, mentioning how usulis examined the attributes of wine and found none alone to be the cause of prohibition. The key lesson is that inductive methods are valuable but fallible tools for discovering causes.

Key Terms
علة
اختلاف
ظن

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why is the method of difference considered better than the method of concordance?
A) It is easier to find two cases that agree in all but one circumstance.
B) It always leads to certainty.
C) It does not require comparing multiple cases.
D) It was developed by John Stuart Mill, a non-Muslim, so it is more objective.

Key Takeaway
The method of difference isolates the 'illa by comparing two cases that are identical except for one circumstance, but it yields only probability, not certainty.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Task 1: In a hadith, the Prophet allowed the sale of dates for dates only in equal measure and hand to hand, but prohibited the sale of dates for other types of fruit in delay. Using the method of difference, design a controlled comparison to determine whether the 'illa is the type of fruit or something else. (Hint: Consider comparing two transactions that differ only in the type of fruit.)
?
Task 2: Evaluate the following claim: 'The method of difference is more reliable than the method of concordance because it yields certainty.' Use the author's own assessment to argue for or against this claim, citing specific reasons from the passage.

The Method of Difference: Identifying Causes by Contrast
Explains the method of difference and its epistemological value

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the method of difference to identify a candidate cause in a two-case comparison and assess its epistemological certainty.

Core Idea
The method of difference isolates cause by comparing two cases that differ in only one factor.

In this lesson, we examine the method of difference (tariqat al-ikhtilaf), a key inductive tool for identifying causes. The author illustrates it with examples and warns that it yields only probable knowledge. We will learn its logical structure and how to apply it.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two cases
Find one case where the phenomenon occurs and one where it does not. Note all known conditions for both cases.
In the passage, the two egg batches and the two matchstick scenarios are such pairs.
2
List identical conditions
Determine which conditions are shared by both cases. These are controlled variables.
For the eggs, all conditions except moisture are identical.
3
Find the differing condition
Identify the one condition that is present when the phenomenon occurs and absent when it does not.
Moisture is present in the successful batch and absent in the unsuccessful one.
4
Conclude the cause with probability
The differing condition is the probable cause. Recognize that the conclusion is only probable due to possible hidden factors.
The author states this method yields only probable preponderance (rujhan zanni).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أما الأولى فقد فقس بيضها وأعطت نتيجة حسنة، وأما الأخرى فقد كانت على عكس ذلك. هنا لا بد أن يتنبه الباحث إلى أن السبب في نجاح عمل الأولى، وجود النسبة المطلوبة من الرطوبة إضافة إلى الشروط الأخرى، وأن السبب في إخفاق عمل الثانية هو عدم وجود النسبة المطلوبة من الرطوبة، مع اتفاق ظروفها مع ظروف الأولى، من كل الوجوه إلا من هذا الوجه. ونمثل لها أيضاً بانطفاء عود الثقاب المشتعل إذا أدخل في إناء مفرغ من الهواء، واستمراره مشتعلاً إذا أدخل في إناء مليء بالهواء، وهنا نلاحظ أن الحالتين متفقتان في كل الظروف، إلا في ظرف واحد هو وجود الهواء عند ظاهرة الاشتعال، وعدم وجوده عند ظاهرة الانطفاء، وهذا يجعلنا نؤكد أن سبب الاشتعال هو وجود الهواء. قيمة هذه الطريقة : هذه الطريقة أيضاً لا تفيد يقيناً علمياً، وإنما تفيد رجحاناً ظنياً فقط، لاحتمال أن يكون الاختلاف في عدد من الأمور الجزئية، وأن يكون سبب الظاهرة في الحقيقة واحداً منها، والأجزاء الأخرى المرافقة متفقة التلازم لا تنفك . وهذه الطريقة لا تخلو من عيوب الطريقة الأولى، ولكنها على كل حال أفضل منها، وذلك لأنه من العسير جداً أن تختلف الحالتان في كل ظروفهما إلا في ظرف واحد، في حين أنه من السهل أن تتفق الحالتان في كل ظروفهما إلا في ظرف واحد. هذه الطريقة هي إحدى طرق استخراج علة الحكم في الفقه الإسلامي. نظر الأصوليون في علة تحريم الخمر، فسبروا الصفات التي تتصف بها هذه المادة، من سيولة، ولون، وكونها من أصل حلو، وغير ذلك، فوجدوا أن شيئاً منها لم تظهر له آثار حرمة في أي شراب آخر لا مفترقاً ولا مجتمعاً، باستثناء وصف واحد انفردت به الخمر، هو كونها مسكرة مفسدة للعقل مضرَّة، فهذا الوصف هو وحده الذي خالفت فيه الخمر الأنواع المباحة من الشراب، فحكموا بأنه هو العلة في التحريم، وأكد ذلك لديهم أنه هو الوصف المناسب لتعليل التحريم، نظراً إلى حكمة الشارع التي تَعْمَد إلى رعاية مصالح الناس. ولما قرروا ذلك، قاسوا ـ قياساً أصولياً ـ على الخمر كل شراب مسكر، وحكموا بتحريمه سواء أكان اسمه خمراً أو لا. وتدخل هذه الطريقة ضمن أنواع «تخريج مناط الحكم» المعروفة في علم أصول الفقه. واستخراج العلة بهذه الطريقة استخراج لها عن طريق العكس.
As for the first, its eggs hatched and gave a good result, while the other was contrary to that. Here the researcher must realize that the reason for the success of the first's operation is the presence of the required proportion of moisture in addition to other conditions, and the reason for the failure of the second's operation is the absence of the required proportion of moisture, with its conditions agreeing with those of the first in all aspects except this one. We also give as an example the extinguishing of a burning matchstick when placed in a vacuum container, and its continued burning when placed in an air-filled container. Here we observe that the two cases agree in all conditions except one condition: the presence of air during the phenomenon of ignition, and its absence during the phenomenon of extinguishing. This makes us affirm that the cause of ignition is the presence of air. Value of this method: This method also does not yield scientific certainty, but only probable preponderance, because it is possible that the difference is in a number of partial matters, and that the cause of the phenomenon is in reality one of them, while the other accompanying parts agree inseparably. This method is not free from the defects of the first method, but it is better than it in any case, because it is very difficult for the two cases to differ in all their conditions except one condition, while it is easy for the two cases to agree in all their conditions except one condition. This method is one of the methods of extracting the cause of a ruling in Islamic jurisprudence. The usul scholars considered the cause of the prohibition of wine, and investigated the attributes characterizing this substance: fluidity, color, being derived from a sweet source, and others. They found that none of them showed effects of prohibition in any other drink, whether separately or combined, except one attribute peculiar to wine: that it is intoxicating, corrupting the mind, and harmful. This attribute alone distinguished wine from permissible types of drink. So they ruled that it is the cause of prohibition. This was confirmed for them by the fact that it is the attribute suitable for justifying the prohibition, given the wisdom of the Lawgiver which tends to care for people's interests. When they established that, they analogized—by usuli analogy—every intoxicating drink to wine, and ruled it prohibited, whether it is called wine or not. This method falls within the types of 'takhrij manat al-hukm' known in the science of usul al-fiqh. Extracting the cause by this method is extraction by way of contrast.
Source pages p. 220

Commentary
This passage defines and illustrates the method of difference (طريقة الاختلاف) as a means of identifying the cause ('illa) of a phenomenon, particularly in Islamic jurisprudence. The author begins by contrasting two cases: one succeeds, the other fails, with all conditions identical except the presence of a specific proportion of moisture. This difference is identified as the cause. A second example using a matchstick in vacuum versus air reinforces the point: the only varying factor is the presence of air, so air is deemed the cause. The author then assesses the method's epistemological value, stating it yields only probable knowledge (رجحان ظني), not certainty, because multiple partial causes could be at play. Despite this limitation, the method is considered superior to the first method (method of agreement) since it is easier to find cases that agree in all respects except one than to find cases that differ in all respects except one. The passage then applies this method to a classical fiqh example: determining the 'illa of wine's prohibition. Usul scholars examined various attributes of wine—fluidity, color, sweetness—and found none universally present in prohibited drinks except intoxication (iskan). They concluded that intoxication is the 'illa (cause of prohibition), as it aligns with the Lawgiver's wisdom of preserving people's interests. This allowed them to apply qiyas (analogy) to all intoxicants. Finally, the method is situated within usul al-fiqh as a form of 'takhrij manat al-hukm' (extracting the basis of a ruling), specifically extraction by way of contrast (عكس).

Key Terms
طريقة الاختلاف
العلة
رجحان ظني

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the epistemological status of the conclusion reached by the method of difference?
A) Scientific certainty (yaqin)
B) Probable preponderance (rujhan zanni)
C) Absolute knowledge
D) No knowledge at all

Key Takeaway
The method of difference identifies a cause by contrasting two cases that are identical except for one varying factor, but its conclusion is only probable.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Consider two similar agricultural plots: one yields sweet dates and the other sour dates. All conditions are identical except that the sweet dates plot receives more sunlight. Apply the method of difference to identify the probable cause of sweetness, and note the epistemic status of your conclusion.
?
In fiqh, suppose two drinks: one is prohibited (khamr) and one is permissible (non-intoxicating nabidh). All other attributes are similar except that only the prohibited drink is intoxicating. Use the method of difference to determine the probable 'illa of prohibition.

Applying the Method of Difference in Usul al-Fiqh: The Wine Example
Applies the method of difference to extract the cause of wine's prohibition

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to reconstruct the usul scholars' application of the method of difference to identify the 'illa of wine's prohibition and explain why intoxication was chosen.

Core Idea
The method of difference isolated intoxication as the unique attribute distinguishing wine from permissible drinks.

In this lesson, we see the method of difference applied to a classical fiqh problem: determining the 'illa (legal cause) for the prohibition of wine. The usul scholars systematically examined attributes of wine and contrasted them with permissible drinks to find the one differentiating factor. This allowed them to extend the ruling to all intoxicants via qiyas.

Guided Path
1
List the attributes of wine
Consider all attributes: fluidity, color, sweetness, being derived from a sweet source, intoxication, etc.
The passage mentions these as attributes considered by usul scholars.
2
Compare with permissible drinks
Check which attributes are present in permissible drinks (e.g., water, juice). Most attributes are shared.
Fluidity, color, sweetness are found in permissible drinks as well.
3
Identify the unique attribute
Find the attribute present only in wine and absent in all permissible drinks.
Intoxication is unique to wine among the compared drinks.
4
Conclude the 'illa
The unique attribute is the probable legal cause ('illa). Confirm its suitability (munasaba) with the ruling.
The passage notes that intoxication is appropriate (munasib) for prohibition given the Lawgiver's wisdom.
5
Apply qiyas
Extend the ruling to other drinks that share the 'illa, i.e., all intoxicants.
This is the standard usuli analogy based on the extracted 'illa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أما الأولى فقد فقس بيضها وأعطت نتيجة حسنة، وأما الأخرى فقد كانت على عكس ذلك. هنا لا بد أن يتنبه الباحث إلى أن السبب في نجاح عمل الأولى، وجود النسبة المطلوبة من الرطوبة إضافة إلى الشروط الأخرى، وأن السبب في إخفاق عمل الثانية هو عدم وجود النسبة المطلوبة من الرطوبة، مع اتفاق ظروفها مع ظروف الأولى، من كل الوجوه إلا من هذا الوجه. ونمثل لها أيضاً بانطفاء عود الثقاب المشتعل إذا أدخل في إناء مفرغ من الهواء، واستمراره مشتعلاً إذا أدخل في إناء مليء بالهواء، وهنا نلاحظ أن الحالتين متفقتان في كل الظروف، إلا في ظرف واحد هو وجود الهواء عند ظاهرة الاشتعال، وعدم وجوده عند ظاهرة الانطفاء، وهذا يجعلنا نؤكد أن سبب الاشتعال هو وجود الهواء. قيمة هذه الطريقة : هذه الطريقة أيضاً لا تفيد يقيناً علمياً، وإنما تفيد رجحاناً ظنياً فقط، لاحتمال أن يكون الاختلاف في عدد من الأمور الجزئية، وأن يكون سبب الظاهرة في الحقيقة واحداً منها، والأجزاء الأخرى المرافقة متفقة التلازم لا تنفك . وهذه الطريقة لا تخلو من عيوب الطريقة الأولى، ولكنها على كل حال أفضل منها، وذلك لأنه من العسير جداً أن تختلف الحالتان في كل ظروفهما إلا في ظرف واحد، في حين أنه من السهل أن تتفق الحالتان في كل ظروفهما إلا في ظرف واحد. هذه الطريقة هي إحدى طرق استخراج علة الحكم في الفقه الإسلامي. نظر الأصوليون في علة تحريم الخمر، فسبروا الصفات التي تتصف بها هذه المادة، من سيولة، ولون، وكونها من أصل حلو، وغير ذلك، فوجدوا أن شيئاً منها لم تظهر له آثار حرمة في أي شراب آخر لا مفترقاً ولا مجتمعاً، باستثناء وصف واحد انفردت به الخمر، هو كونها مسكرة مفسدة للعقل مضرَّة، فهذا الوصف هو وحده الذي خالفت فيه الخمر الأنواع المباحة من الشراب، فحكموا بأنه هو العلة في التحريم، وأكد ذلك لديهم أنه هو الوصف المناسب لتعليل التحريم، نظراً إلى حكمة الشارع التي تَعْمَد إلى رعاية مصالح الناس. ولما قرروا ذلك، قاسوا ـ قياساً أصولياً ـ على الخمر كل شراب مسكر، وحكموا بتحريمه سواء أكان اسمه خمراً أو لا. وتدخل هذه الطريقة ضمن أنواع «تخريج مناط الحكم» المعروفة في علم أصول الفقه. واستخراج العلة بهذه الطريقة استخراج لها عن طريق العكس.

We also give as an example the extinguishing of a burning matchstick when placed in a vacuum container, and its continued burning when placed in an air-filled container. Here we observe that the two cases agree in all conditions except one condition: the presence of air during the phenomenon of ignition, and its absence during the phenomenon of extinguishing. This makes us affirm that the cause of ignition is the presence of air. Value of this method: This method also does not yield scientific certainty, but only probable preponderance, because it is possible that the difference is in a number of partial matters, and that the cause of the phenomenon is in reality one of them, while the other accompanying parts agree inseparably. This method is not free from the defects of the first method, but it is better than it in any case, because it is very difficult for the two cases to differ in all their conditions except one condition, while it is easy for the two cases to agree in all their conditions except one condition. This method is one of the methods of extracting the cause of a ruling in Islamic jurisprudence. The usul scholars considered the cause of the prohibition of wine, and investigated the attributes characterizing this substance: fluidity, color, being derived from a sweet source, and others. They found that none of them showed effects of prohibition in any other drink, whether separately or combined, except one attribute peculiar to wine: that it is intoxicating, corrupting the mind, and harmful. This attribute alone distinguished wine from permissible types of drink. So they ruled that it is the cause of prohibition. This was confirmed for them by the fact that it is the attribute suitable for justifying the prohibition, given the wisdom of the Lawgiver which tends to care for people's interests. When they established that, they analogized—by usuli analogy—every intoxicating drink to wine, and ruled it prohibited, whether it is called wine or not. This method falls within the types of 'takhrij manat al-hukm' known in the science of usul al-fiqh. Extracting the cause by this method is extraction by way of contrast.
Source pages p. 220

Commentary
This passage defines and illustrates the method of difference (طريقة الاختلاف) as a means of identifying the cause ('illa) of a phenomenon, particularly in Islamic jurisprudence. The author begins by contrasting two cases: one succeeds, the other fails, with all conditions identical except the presence of a specific proportion of moisture. This difference is identified as the cause. A second example using a matchstick in vacuum versus air reinforces the point: the only varying factor is the presence of air, so air is deemed the cause. The author then assesses the method's epistemological value, stating it yields only probable knowledge (رجحان ظني), not certainty, because multiple partial causes could be at play. Despite this limitation, the method is considered superior to the first method (method of agreement) since it is easier to find cases that agree in all respects except one than to find cases that differ in all respects except one. The passage then applies this method to a classical fiqh example: determining the 'illa of wine's prohibition. Usul scholars examined various attributes of wine—fluidity, color, sweetness—and found none universally present in prohibited drinks except intoxication (iskan). They concluded that intoxication is the 'illa (cause of prohibition), as it aligns with the Lawgiver's wisdom of preserving people's interests. This allowed them to apply qiyas (analogy) to all intoxicants. Finally, the method is situated within usul al-fiqh as a form of 'takhrij manat al-hukm' (extracting the basis of a ruling), specifically extraction by way of contrast (عكس).

Key Terms
طريقة الاختلاف
العلة
تخريج مناط الحكم

The Joint Method of Agreement and Difference
Introduces the combined method of agreement and difference for inductive inference.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the combined method of agreement and difference to test a causal hypothesis in inductive reasoning.

Core Idea
Combining agreement and difference besieges the hypothesis from two sides.

This lesson presents the third inductive method, which strengthens causal inference by simultaneously checking positive and negative cases. The method is a cornerstone of inductive logic in Islamic jurisprudence (usul al-fiqh) for identifying effective causes. By examining both when the phenomenon occurs and when it does not, the researcher can confidently isolate the true cause.

Guided Path
1
Extract the circumstance common to all positive cases
Identify the circumstance (ظرف) that is present whenever the phenomenon occurs. This is the method of agreement.
Ensure that other circumstances vary; the constant one is the candidate cause.
2
Test the negative cases
Find cases where the phenomenon is absent. Check if the candidate cause is also absent, while other circumstances remain.
If the cause is absent when the phenomenon is absent, it passes the difference test.
3
Combine both results
If the candidate cause is present in all positive cases and absent in all negative cases, the hypothesis is strongly supported.
This joint method is more rigorous than either alone.
4
Apply to an Islamic legal example
In usul al-fiqh, to identify the 'illah (cause) of a ruling, list cases where the ruling applies and where it does not. The common factor in affirmative cases and absent in negative cases is the 'illah.
For example, the prohibition of khamr (wine) due to intoxication.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
٣ - شرح الطريقة الثالثة : وهي النظر في الاتفاق والاختلاف معاً. وهذه الطريقة تجمع بين الطريقتين السابقتين، فتنظر إلى حالات الظاهرة، وتستخرج الظرف الذي اتفقت عليه الحالات، فلم يفارق في أية حالة منها مع أن الظروف الأخرى وجدت وتخلفت، ثم تتأكد بدراسة أخرى من تخلف وجود الظاهرة عند تخلف وجود هذا الظرف نفسه، مع وجود الظروف الأخرى. وبهذه الطريقة تحاصر الدراسة الاستقرائية الفرض عن طريقي الاتفاق والاختلاف، للتأكد من أنه هو السبب في حدوث الظاهرة، أو يشتمل على السبب. أمثلة على تطبيق هذه الطريقة : ١ - ظهر في أحد المصانع انخفاض في الإنتاج بنسبة ملحوظة جداً، فاستدعى مدير المصنع المختص عن متابعة الإنتاج، وسأله عن سبب هذا الانخفاض.
3. Explanation of the third method: It is considering agreement and difference together. This method combines the two preceding methods. It examines the cases of the phenomenon and extracts the circumstance on which the cases agreed, which did not depart in any case, while other circumstances existed and were absent. Then it confirms by another study that the phenomenon is absent when this circumstance itself is absent, while other circumstances are present. By this method, the inductive study besieges the hypothesis through the ways of agreement and difference, to confirm that it is the cause of the phenomenon's occurrence, or contains the cause. Examples of applying this method: 1. There appeared in a factory a very noticeable decrease in production, so the factory manager summoned the person in charge of production follow-up and asked him about the reason for this decrease.
Source pages p. 221

Commentary
This passage introduces the third method of inductive reasoning, which combines the method of agreement (طريقة الاتفاق) and the method of difference (طريقة الاختلاف). The author explains that this integrated approach works in two steps: first, one examines instances where the phenomenon occurs and identifies a circumstance that is present in all such instances (agreement). Second, one verifies by another study that when this circumstance is absent, the phenomenon is also absent, while other circumstances remain present (difference). This dual testing 'besieges' the hypothesis, making it more likely to be the true cause. The author then begins an example from a factory where production declined, but the example is cut off in the provided text. The method is essentially the 'Joint Method of Agreement and Difference' known in modern inductive logic, adapted here to Islamic contexts such as fiqh and empirical investigation. The passage emphasizes that this method provides stronger evidence than either method alone.

Method of 'Aks: Extracting the 'Illa by Exclusion
Author explains extraction of 'illa by 'aks using khamr example

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the method of 'aks to identify the effective cause ('illa) of a legal ruling and construct a valid analogical argument (qiyas usuli).

Core Idea
The 'illa is the unique description absent when the ruling is absent.

In usul al-fiqh, identifying the effective cause (al-‘illa) behind a legal ruling is essential for extending that ruling to new cases. One powerful method for finding the ‘illa is al-‘aks (the inverse), where you isolate the one description that uniquely corresponds to the ruling: when that description is present, the ruling applies; when absent, the ruling disappears. The classic example of this method is the case of khamr (wine), whose prohibition is attributed to its intoxicating quality. This lesson walks you through the logical steps of that method and shows how it grounds analogical reasoning in Islamic law.

Guided Path
1
List all descriptions of the original case
Begin by enumerating every characteristic of the original case (al-asl) that could plausibly be connected to the ruling. For khamr, these include its red colour, grape origin, intoxicating effect, harmfulness, etc.
The goal is to be exhaustive; no description should be assumed irrelevant prematurely.
2
Eliminate descriptions shared with permissible cases
Compare the original case with similar permissible objects. Remove any description that is also found in a case where the ruling does not apply. For khamr, all descriptions except intoxication are shared with lawful drinks.
This is the core of ‘aks: what remains after elimination is the candidate ‘illa.
3
Identify the unique description
The description that is exclusive to the original case and absent in all permissible analogues is the likely ‘illa. In the khamr example, only the intoxicating-corrupting-harmful nature is unique.
Uniqueness alone is not enough; the description must also be suitable (munasib) for the ruling's purpose.
4
Test suitability with the Lawgiver's wisdom
Verify that the identified description aligns with the Lawgiver’s general purposes (maqasid al-shari‘a). Intoxication is suitable because it destroys intellect, which the Lawgiver seeks to protect.
Suitability strengthens the case that this is the true ‘illa.
5
Apply the ‘illa to new cases via qiyas usuli
Once the ‘illa is established, any new case sharing that ‘illa receives the same ruling. Thus every intoxicating drink, regardless of name, is prohibited by analogy to khamr.
This step converts the ‘aks method into a fully valid analogical argument.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باستثناء وصف واحد انفردت به الخمر، هو كونها مسكرة مفسدة للعقل مُضرَّة، فهذا الوصف هو وحده الذي خالفت فيه الخمر الأنواع المباحة من الشراب، فحكموا بأنه هو العلة في التحريم، وأكد ذلك لديهم أنه هو الوصف المناسب لتعليل التحريم، نظراً إلى حكمة الشارع التي تَعْمَد إلى رعاية مصالح الناس. ولما قرروا ذلك، قاسوا ـ قياساً أصولياً ـ على الخمر كل شراب مسكر، وحكموا بتحريمه سواء أكان اسمه خمراً أو لا. وتدخل هذه الطريقة ضمن أنواع «تخريج مناط الحكم» المعروفة في علم أصول الفقه. واستخراج العلة بهذه الطريقة استخراج لها عن طريق العكس.
With the exception of one description unique to khamr, which is that it is intoxicating, corrupting the mind, and harmful. So this description alone is that by which khamr differs from the permissible types of drink. Thus they ruled that it is the cause (illa) of prohibition, and that was confirmed for them because it is the description suitable for justifying the prohibition, considering the wisdom of the Lawgiver which tends to safeguard the interests of people. When they established that, they analogized (using legal analogy) to khamr every intoxicating drink, and ruled it prohibited whether its name is khamr or not. This method falls under the types of 'takhrij manat al-hukm' known in the science of usul al-fiqh. Extracting the cause by this method is extraction via the inverse (aks).

Commentary
This passage describes the method of 'aks (inverse) used in usul al-fiqh to identify the effective cause (illa) of a legal ruling. The author explains this by examining the example of khamr (wine). The scholars observed that khamr has many descriptions, but the only one that distinguishes it from permissible beverages is its intoxicating, mind-corrupting, harmful nature. This unique description is therefore the cause of prohibition. This is confirmed by its suitability ('suitability' meaning it aligns with the Lawgiver's purpose of preserving people's interests). Having established this, they then apply legal analogy (qiyas usuli) to all intoxicating drinks, ruling them prohibited regardless of name. The author notes that this approach is a type of 'takhrij manat al-hukm' (deriving the effective cause), and that extracting the cause through this method is called extraction by 'aks (inverse or exclusion). In logic, 'aks often means conversion, but here it refers to isolating the cause by eliminating all other descriptions.

Method of Agreement and Difference for Causal Discovery
Author explains the third method combining agreement and difference to discover causes, with a factory productivity example.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the method of agreement and difference to identify a causal factor in Islamic legal reasoning (e.g., determining the 'illah in qiyas).

Core Idea
Certainty in causation requires both agreement of presence and agreement of absence.

In the previous lessons, you learned about the method of agreement (ittifāq) and the method of difference (ikhtilāf) separately. Each alone can suggest a cause, but to achieve near-certainty, Islamic logicians and jurists combine both. This lesson introduces the third method that merges both approaches, which is especially powerful in inductive investigations, such as establishing the effective cause ('illah) for analogical reasoning in fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the phenomenon (ẓāhir)
Clearly define the phenomenon you want to explain (e.g., low production, or a legal ruling). This is the effect whose cause you seek.
2
Find the common circumstance in positive cases (ittifāq)
Examine all instances where the phenomenon occurs. List all circumstances (ẓurūf) present in each case. Identify the one circumstance that is present in every case without exception. This is the 'agreement' step.
3
Check the absence of that circumstance in negative cases (ikhtilāf)
Now examine instances where the phenomenon does not occur. Verify that the circumstance identified in step 2 is absent from all these negative cases. If any negative case contains the circumstance, then the hypothesis is weakened.
4
Conclude causation
If a single circumstance is present in all positive cases and absent in all negative cases, you have strong evidence that this circumstance is either the cause or contains the cause. In Islamic legal induction, this is the basis for establishing 'illah.
The author notes that this method yields 'knowledge resembling certainty' (maʿrifa shabīha bil-yaqīn).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
٣ - شرح الطريقة الثالثة : وهي النظر في الاتفاق والاختلاف معاً. وهذه الطريقة تجمع بين الطريقتين السابقتين، فتنظر إلى حالات الظاهرة، وتستخرج الظرف الذي اتفقت عليه الحالات، فلم يفارق في أية حالة منها مع أن الظروف الأخرى وجدت وتخلفت، ثم تتأكد بدراسة أخرى من تخلف وجود الظاهرة عند تخلف وجود هذا الظرف نفسه، مع وجود الظروف الأخرى. وبهذه الطريقة تحاصر الدراسة الاستقرائية الفرض عن طريقي الاتفاق والاختلاف، للتأكد من أنه هو السبب في حدوث الظاهرة، أو يشتمل على السبب. أمثلة على تطبيق هذه الطريقة : ١ - ظهر في أحد المصانع انخفاض في الإنتاج بنسبة ملحوظة جداً، فاستدعى مدير المصنع المختص عن متابعة الإنتاج، وسأله عن سبب هذا الانخفاض. عندئذ أسرع المختص الباحث فصنف عمال المصنع إلى وحدات، بحسب نسبة إنتاج الأفراد، ثم انتزع مجموعة أفراد الوحدة الدنيا ذات الإنتاج المنخفض جداً، واستقدمها إليه ليدرس ظروف كل فرد منها، ويعرف سبب ضعف إنتاجها، واعتبر كل فرد من هذه المجموعة حالة من الحالات، واعتبر واقع كل فرد ظروفه، صحية كانت أو نفسية أو اقتصادية أو غير ذلك. وبدراسة ظروف أفراد هذه المجموعة، لم يجد ظرفاً مشتركاً بينهم جميعاً إلا ظرفاً واحداً هو (تناولهم المخدرات)، أما ظروفهم الأخرى فلم يتفق ظرف منها أن اشترك فيه الجميع. فاستخرج هذا الظرف الذي اتفقت عليه جميع الحالات وهو: (تناول المخدرات). هذه هي العملية الأولى. ثم أجرى العملية الثانية فانتزع مجموعة من أفراد الوحدة العليا ذات الإنتاج الكثير، واستقدمها إليه ليدرس ظروف كل فرد منها، واعتبر كل فرد من هذه المجموعة حالة من الحالات، واعتبر واقع كل فرد ظروفه. ولدى دراسة ظروف أفراد هذه المجموعة وجد أن الظرف الوحيد الذي تخلف من أفرادها جميعاً هو (تناول المخدرات). فإن أحداً من هؤلاء الأفراد لا يتناول شيئاً من المخدرات. فاستخرج هذا الظرف الوحيد الذي تخلف وجود الظاهرة لدى تخلفه، فكان هو الذي وجدت الظاهرة لدى وجوده. ومن هاتين العمليتين معاً عرف معرفة شبيهة باليقين أن السبب في ضعف إنتاج المصنع هو تناول بعض عماله المخدرات. ٢ - دولة من الدول كثرت الجرائم في بعض بلدانها، ولمعرفة كثرة الجرائم هذه وضعت الفروض التالية: الأمية - الفقر - عدم رقابة جهاز الأمن - قلتهم - عدم وجود العقوبات الزاجرة - ضعف الوازع الديني.
3 - Explanation of the third method: It is considering agreement and difference together. This method combines the two previous methods. It examines the instances of the phenomenon and extracts the circumstance that all instances agree upon, which is not absent in any instance even though other circumstances are present and absent. Then it confirms by another study of the absence of the phenomenon when this same circumstance is absent, while other circumstances are present. In this way, the inductive study besieges the hypothesis through both agreement and difference, to confirm that it is the cause of the occurrence of the phenomenon, or contains the cause. Examples of applying this method: 1 - In one factory, a very significant decline in production appeared. The factory manager called the specialist responsible for production monitoring and asked him about the reason for this decline. Thereupon, the specialist researcher quickly classified the factory workers into units according to the individuals' production rates. Then he took a group of individuals from the lowest unit with very low production and summoned them to study the circumstances of each individual and know the reason for their weak production. He considered each individual in this group as a case, and considered the reality of each individual as his circumstances, whether health-related, psychological, economic, or otherwise. By studying the circumstances of the individuals in this group, he did not find any circumstance common to all of them except one circumstance: (their consumption of drugs). As for their other circumstances, none of them agreed to be shared by all. So he extracted this circumstance that all cases agreed upon, which is: (drug consumption). This is the first operation. Then he carried out the second operation: he took a group of individuals from the highest unit with high production and summoned them to study the circumstances of each individual. He considered each individual in this group as a case, and considered the reality of each individual as his circumstances. Upon studying the circumstances of the individuals in this group, he found that the only circumstance absent from all of them is (drug consumption). For none of these individuals consume any drugs. So he extracted this single circumstance whose absence coincided with the absence of the phenomenon, and whose presence coincided with the presence of the phenomenon. From both these operations together, he gained knowledge resembling certainty that the cause of the weak production in the factory is the consumption of drugs by some of its workers. 2 - In a country, crimes increased in some of its regions. To determine the reason for this increase in crimes, the following hypotheses were proposed: illiteracy, poverty, lack of surveillance by the security apparatus, their small number, absence of deterrent penalties, weakness of religious deterrent.
Source pages p. 221

Commentary
This passage explains the third method for discovering causes, which combines agreement and difference. It is an inductive method. The author begins by describing the method: first, examine all instances where the phenomenon occurs and find the single circumstance they all share (agreement). Second, examine instances where the phenomenon does not occur and see if that same circumstance is absent (difference). If the circumstance is present in all occurrence cases and absent in all non-occurrence cases, it is likely the cause. The author then provides a concrete example from a factory. In the first operation, the researcher identified a low-production group, studied their circumstances, and found drug consumption was the only common factor. In the second operation, he studied a high-production group and found drug consumption was absent in all of them. Thus, by agreement and difference, drug consumption was identified as the cause of low production. The passage also begins a second example about crime rates, listing possible hypotheses such as illiteracy, poverty, etc., but the example is cut off.

The Third Method: Dawaran in Causal Inference
Explains the third method of causal inference combining agreement and difference, linking to usul al-fiqh.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the method of correlation (dawaran) to identify the 'illa in a legal ruling by checking both presence and absence.

Core Idea
Correlation of existence and non-existence strongly indicates causality, but not certainty.

This lesson introduces the third method of causal inference, which combines agreement and difference. You will see how this method is used in both general scientific reasoning and in Islamic legal theory (usul al-fiqh) to identify the effective cause ('illa) of a ruling. The passage calls this method 'al-tariqa al-thalitha' and equates it with the classical fiqh principle of 'dawaran al-'illa ma'a al-ma'lul'.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two operations
The method has two phases: first, find a common factor in multiple cases where the phenomenon exists (method of agreement). Second, confirm that this factor is absent in cases where the phenomenon is absent (method of difference). Together, they form a stronger inference.
2
Trace the factory example
Follow the researcher: he selects low-production workers and finds they all use drugs (agreement). Then he selects high-production workers and finds none use drugs (difference). The drug use tracks production level, so it is the likely cause.
3
Assess strength and limitations
The passage states the third method is stronger than either alone (two witnesses are better than one) but still yields only strong probability, not certainty. The same defects of the individual methods apply, albeit reduced.
4
Connect to usul al-fiqh: dawaran
In Islamic legal theory, this method is called 'dawaran al-'illa ma'a al-ma'lul wujudan wa 'adaman'. It means: when the attribute (wasf) exists, the ruling exists; when it is absent, the ruling is absent. This correlation is a strong indicator that the attribute is the 'illa.
For example, the 'illa for the prohibition of wine is intoxication: when intoxication is present, the ruling applies; when absent (as in vinegar), it does not.
