عندئذ أسرع المختص الباحث فصنف عمال المصنع إلى وحدات، بحسب نسبة إنتاج الأفراد، ثم انتزع مجموعة أفراد الوحدة الدنيا ذات الإنتاج المنخفض جداً، واستقدمها إليه ليدرس ظروف كل فرد منها، ويعرف سبب ضعف إنتاجها، واعتبر كل فرد من هذه المجموعة حالة من الحالات، واعتبر واقع كل فرد ظروفه، صحية كانت أو نفسية أو اقتصادية أو غير ذلك. وبدراسة ظروف أفراد هذه المجموعة، لم يجد ظرفاً مشتركاً بينهم جميعاً إلا ظرفاً واحداً هو (تناولهم المخدرات)، أما ظروفهم الأخرى فلم يتفق ظرف منها أن اشترك فيه الجميع. فاستخرج هذا الظرف الذي اتفقت عليه جميع الحالات وهو: (تناول المخدرات). هذه هي العملية الأولى. ثم أجرى العملية الثانية فانتزع مجموعة من أفراد الوحدة العليا ذات الإنتاج الكثير، واستقدمها إليه ليدرس ظروف كل فرد منها، واعتبر كل فرد من هذه المجموعة حالة من الحالات، واعتبر واقع كل فرد ظروفه. ولدى دراسة ظروف أفراد هذه المجموعة وجد أن الظرف الوحيد الذي تخلف من أفرادها جميعاً هو (تناول المخدرات). فإن أحداً من هؤلاء الأفراد لا يتناول شيئاً من المخدرات. فاستخرج هذا الظرف الوحيد الذي تخلف وجود الظاهرة لدى تخلفه، فكان هو الذي وجدت الظاهرة لدى وجوده. ومن هاتين العمليتين معاً عرف معرفة شبيهة باليقين أن السبب في ضعف إنتاج المصنع هو تناول بعض عماله المخدرات. ٢ - دولة من الدول كثرت الجرائم في بعض بلدانها، ولمعرفة كثرة الجرائم هذه وضعت الفروض التالية: الأمية - الفقر - عدم رقابة جهاز الأمن - قلتهم - عدم وجود العقوبات الزاجرة - ضعف الوازع الديني. ولدى الموازنة بين البلدان التي تكثر فيها الجرائم، والبلدان الأخرى التي تقل فيها الجرائم، تبين أن معظم أفراد البلدان التي تكثر فيها الجرائم لا يتفقون في شيء إلا في ضعف الوازع الديني، وأن معظم أفراد البلدان الأخرى التي تقلّ فيها الجرائم لم يختلفوا في شيء عن ظروف أفراد البلدان السابقة إلا في قوة الوازع الديني. ومن دراسة الحالتين معاً تبين لنا وجود الظاهرة عند وجود السبب، وانعدام الظاهرة عند انعدام السبب. قيمة هذه الطريقة: باعتبار أنها تجمع بين الطريقتين الأولى والثانية لا بد أن تكون أقوى من كل منهما، لأن شاهدين أقوى من شاهد، والاستدلال بالطريقتين أقوى من الاستدلال بإحداهما بداهة. ومع ذلك فهي لا تقدم يقيناً علمياً، وإنما تقدم ظناً مؤكد الرجحان. والعيوب التي ذكرت في كل من الطريقتين الأولى والثانية؛ تذكر في الطريقة الثالثة الجامعة لهما معاً، ولكن تخفُّ نسبة احتمال بطلان نتائجها بقدر القوة المضافة بسبب الاجتماع. هذه الطريقة هي إحدى طرق استخراج علة الحكم في الفقه الإسلامي. إن ما جاء في هذه الطريقة هو المعروف عند علماء أصول الفقه الإسلامي، بدوران العلة مع المعلول وجوداً وعدماً، فمن أدلة العليّة القوية عندهم هذا الدوران أي: وجود الحكم عند وجود الوصف، وانعدام الحكم عند انعدام الوصف. ومن الدوران يستنبطون أن الوصف الدائر الذي يلزم من وجوده وجود الحكم، ومن انعدامه انعدام الحكم، هو العلة في الحكم.
Then the specialist researcher quickly classified the factory workers into units according to the ratio of individual production, then extracted the group of individuals of the lowest unit with very low production, and brought them to him to study the conditions of each individual and know the cause of their weak production, and considered each individual of this group as a case, and considered the reality of each individual as his conditions, whether health, psychological, economic or otherwise. And by studying the conditions of the individuals of this group, he did not find a common condition among all of them except one condition: (their consumption of drugs). As for their other conditions, no condition agreed that all shared it. So he extracted this condition which all cases agreed upon: (drug consumption). This is the first operation. Then he performed the second operation: he extracted a group of individuals from the highest unit with high production, and brought them to him to study the conditions of each individual, and considered each individual of this group as a case, and considered the reality of each individual as his conditions. And upon studying the conditions of the individuals of this group, he found that the only condition absent from all its individuals was (drug consumption). For not one of these individuals consumes any drugs. So he extracted this single condition which the phenomenon was absent when it was absent, and it was the one with which the phenomenon existed when it existed. And from these two operations together he knew with knowledge resembling certainty that the cause of the weak production of the factory was the consumption of drugs by some of its workers. 2 - A state where crimes increased in some of its countries, and to know this increase in crime the following hypotheses were set: illiteracy, poverty, lack of security agency surveillance, their scarcity, absence of deterrent penalties, weakness of religious conscience. And upon balancing between the countries where crimes are frequent and the other countries where crimes are few, it became clear that most individuals of the countries where crimes are frequent do not agree on anything except the weakness of religious conscience, and that most individuals of the other countries where crimes are few did not differ in anything from the conditions of the individuals of the previous countries except in the strength of religious conscience. And from studying both cases together, we saw the existence of the phenomenon when the cause exists, and the absence of the phenomenon when the cause is absent. The value of this method: Considering that it combines the first and second methods, it must be stronger than each of them, because two witnesses are stronger than one, and reasoning by both methods is stronger than reasoning by one of them obviously. Nevertheless, it does not provide scientific certainty, but rather provides a strongly probable opinion. And the defects mentioned in each of the first and second methods are mentioned in the third method that combines them both, but the probability of its results being invalid is reduced by the amount of strength added due to the combination. This method is one of the methods of extracting the cause of a ruling in Islamic jurisprudence. What is presented in this method is known to scholars of Islamic legal theory as the correlation of the cause with the effect in existence and non-existence. For among the strong evidences of causality for them is this correlation, i.e., the existence of the ruling when the attribute exists, and the absence of the ruling when the attribute is absent. And from the correlation they deduce that the circling attribute, whose existence necessitates the existence of the ruling and whose absence necessitates the absence of the ruling, is the cause of the ruling.
Source pages p. 222

Commentary
This passage explains a method of causal inference known as the 'third method' (al-tariqa al-thalitha), which combines the method of agreement and the method of difference. The author first illustrates with a factory example: the researcher identifies low-production workers, finds a common factor (drug use); then examines high-production workers, finds the absence of that factor; thus concludes drug use causes low production. Then a second example: comparing crime-ridden countries with low-crime countries reveals the common factor is weakness of religious conscience. The passage then discusses the value of this combined method: it is stronger than either alone because two witnesses are stronger than one, but it only yields strong probability, not certainty. The defects of the individual methods still apply but are reduced. Finally, the author connects this to Islamic legal theory (usul al-fiqh), where it is known as 'dawaran al-'illa ma'a al-ma'lul wujudan wa 'adaman' (correlation of the cause with the effect in existence and non-existence). In fiqh, scholars use this correlation as a strong indicator that a certain attribute (wasf) is the 'illa (cause) of a legal ruling. The passage thus defines this inductive method and situates it within the Islamic legal tradition.

Key Terms
الطريقة الثالثة (al-ṭarīqa al-thālitha): The method that combines the method of agreement (first) and method of difference (second) for causal inference; it is stronger than either alone but yields only probability. [Note: No significant shift – this is a modern logical term, but the underlying concept is the same as dawaran in classical usul al-fiqh.]
دوران العلة مع المعلول (dawarān al-ʿilla maʿa al-maʿlūl): The correlation of the cause with the effect: the ruling exists when the attribute exists and is absent when the attribute is absent; a strong indicator of causality in Islamic legal theory. [Note: This term is stable in usul al-fiqh across classical and modern texts.]
العلة (al-ʿilla): The cause (in legal theory) that brings about a ruling; here identified through the correlation of existence and non-existence. [Note: No significant shift – 'illa in usul al-fiqh consistently means the effective cause.]

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Dawaran al-'illa ma'a al-ma'lul wujudan wa 'adaman
C) Istiqra' al-'illa
D) Qiyas al-'illa

Key Takeaway
The third method combines presence and absence to strongly indicate causality, but remains probabilistic; in usul al-fiqh it is called dawaran and is a key tool for identifying the 'illa.

Induction and Analogy
intermediate

Method of Concomitant Variation and Its Applications
Author defines the method of concomitant variation with scientific and shar'i examples.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the method of concomitant variation in an inductive argument and apply it to an Islamic legal example.

Core Idea
Concomitant variation shows causality when effect proportionally follows cause.

The method of concomitant variation is a powerful inductive tool for establishing causal relationships. Unlike simpler methods that only check for presence or absence of a cause, this method tracks how changes in the cause correspond to proportional changes in the effect. In this lesson, you will see how the author defines this method using an analogy, a scientific example from Pasteur's germ theory, and a shar'i example linking responsibility to voluntary capacity. Mastering this method will sharpen your ability to evaluate causal claims in both natural and religious sciences.

Guided Path
1
Identify the cause and effect in the key analogy
In the analogy of the keys, the cause is turning the fuel key, and the effect is the level of ignition (increase, decrease, extinction). Observe that other keys do not produce this effect.
2
Extract the three conditions of the method
The method requires existence (cause present -> effect present), absence (cause absent -> effect absent), and proportional variation (increase in cause quantity -> increase in effect quantity; decrease similarly).
3
Apply to Pasteur's germ experiment
Identify the cause (presence of germs in air) and effect (decomposition). Note how in rural areas (more germs) decomposition was high, and in high altitude (fewer germs) decomposition was low, confirming proportional variation.
4
Apply to the shar'i example of responsibility
The cause is voluntary capacity (al-kasb al-iradi), and the effect is legal responsibility. The passage shows that when capacity is absent (insanity, sleep, etc.), responsibility is removed; when capacity increases (greater intellectual/physical abilities), responsibility increases.
5
Distinguish from other inductive methods
Unlike the methods of agreement and difference which only check presence/absence, concomitant variation adds proportional change, providing stronger evidence for causation.

المفاتيح اللولبية التي تتناقص وتتزايد في العطاء، وهذه المفاتيح مجهولة الوظائف بالنسبة إلينا، فبعضها للوقود، وبعضها للهواء، وبعضها للماء، وبعضها له وظائف أخرى، ونحن نريد أن نعرف مفتاح الوقود لنتحكم تكاثر وجود كمية الظاهرة موازية لنسبة تكاثر وجود كمية السبب، ونسبة تناقص وجود كمية الظاهرة موازية لنسبة تناقص وجود كمية السبب . ففي هذه الطريقة إضافة شاهد مرجّح جديد على طريقة الاتفاق والاختلاف معاً، التعفّن يرجع إلى وجود حيوانات دقيقة جداً تتناثر مع الذرات الصغيرة، ويحملها الهواء فتقع على الأجسام والسوائل فتتغذى بها وتتكاثر . وقد نقض «باستير» بنظريته هذه، الفكرة التي كانت سائدة من قبل، والتي كانت ترى أنه قد تتولد كائنات حيّة دون أن تشتق من كائنات حية . ولتحقيق «باستير» ما افترضه، أخذ في أول الأمر أنبوبتين ووضع في كلتيهما كميتين متساويتين من محلول السكر، وعقمهما في ماء تزيد درجة حرارته على ١٠٠ سنتيجراد، ثم أغلق فوهة إحداهما وترك الأخرى مفتوحة ومعرضة للهواء ووضعهما في ظروف متماثلة تماماً عدا هذين الظرفين. وبعد مدة من الزمن فحص السائلين، فوجد أن المفتوحة منهما هي التي بدأت تتعفن، وأما المغلقة فظلت محافظة على وضعها السليم، فتأكد بطريقة الاختلاف، أن التعفن ناشيء عن حيوانات دقيقة جداً يحملها الهواء فتنتقل إلى المواد القابلة للتعفن، وتتكاثر متغذية بها. ثم تابع تأكده فاستخدم طريقة التغير النسبي، فأخذ ثلاث مجموعات من الأنابيب، عدد كل منها عشرون أنبوبة، ثم ملأها بسائل معين، ثم عقم الأنابيب، وأغلق فوهاتها جميعاً، ثم وضع كل مجموعة في مكان معين، ثم فتحها في أمكنتها. وبعد مدة من الزمن وجد أن نسبة التعفن قد اختلفت باختلاف نسبة الرياح الحاملة للجراثيم، وأن زيادة التعفن كانت ملازمة لزيادة نسبة الجراثيم في الهواء، وذلك حين يكون الهواء أكثر تعرضاً للتلوث بالجراثيم، كمناطق الريف، وأن تناقص التعفن كان ملازماً لتناقص نسبة الجراثيم في الهواء، كالمناطق المرتفعة، والمناطق ذات الجليد الدائم، وهي المناطق التي وزع فيها «باستير» أنابيب التجربة. ومن أمثلة تطبيق هذه الطريقة في الشرعيات موضوع ارتباط مسؤولية الإنسان باستطاعته وبكسبه الإرادي، واعتبار هذا الكسب الإرادي المستطاع هو السبب في المسؤولية. ويستدل للتحقق من هذا السبب، بتقرير محاسبته على مقدار نيته في العمل، بالثواب أو بالعقاب، وبرفع المؤاخذة عنه في حالات الجنون حتى يفيق، والنوم حتى يستيقظ، والنسيان حتى يتذكر، وفي حالات الإكراه، وبتزايد مسؤوليته بمقدار تزايد خصائصه وقدراته الفكرية والجسدية والنفسية.
The spiral keys that decrease and increase in supply, and these keys are unknown in function to us, some for fuel, some for air, some for water, and some for other functions, and we want to know the fuel key to control the proportion of energy supply to the oven. So if we assume that one of them is the fuel key, we could conduct the method of verifying the relative change. Then if the increase and decrease of ignition to the point of extinction are linked to the assumed key, and this phenomenon does not occur by moving the other keys, that is evidence that it is the cause connecting to the fuel energy. In this method it becomes clear to us the existence of the phenomenon when the cause exists, and the absence of the phenomenon when the cause is absent, and the proportion of the increase in the quantity of the phenomenon is parallel to the proportion of the increase in the quantity of the cause, and the proportion of the decrease in the quantity of the phenomenon is parallel to the proportion of the decrease in the quantity of the cause. So in this method there is an additional probable indicator alongside the method of agreement and difference together, which is the method of relative change. Among the examples of applying this method is what the French scientist Pasteur conducted when he wanted to verify his theory of germs. The story is that Pasteur announced that every living organism is generated from another living organism, and that decomposition is due to the presence of very minute animals scattered with small particles, carried by air, falling on bodies and liquids, feeding on them and multiplying. Pasteur refuted with this theory the previously prevailing idea that living organisms could be generated without deriving from living organisms. To verify what he hypothesized, Pasteur first took two tubes and placed in both equal amounts of sugar solution, sterilized them in water at a temperature above 100 degrees Celsius, then sealed the mouth of one and left the other open and exposed to air, placing them in completely identical conditions except for these two circumstances. After a period of time he examined the liquids and found that the open one had started to decompose, while the sealed one remained intact, thus confirming by the method of difference that decomposition arises from very minute animals carried by air that transfer to decomposable materials and multiply by feeding on them. Then he continued his confirmation and used the method of relative change, taking three groups of tubes, each group consisting of twenty tubes, then filled them with a specific liquid, sterilized the tubes, sealed all their mouths, then placed each group in a specific location, then opened them in their places. After a period of time he found that the proportion of decomposition differed according to the proportion of winds carrying germs, and that the increase in decomposition was concomitant with the increase in the proportion of germs in the air, such as when the air is more exposed to contamination by germs, like rural areas, and that the decrease in decomposition was concomitant with the decrease in the proportion of germs in the air, like high altitudes and permanently frozen regions, which were the areas where Pasteur distributed the experimental tubes. Among the examples of applying this method in legal matters is the subject of linking human responsibility to his ability and his voluntary acquisition, and considering this voluntary acquired ability as the cause of responsibility. Evidence for verifying this cause is by establishing his accountability according to the amount of his intention in the deed, by reward or punishment, and the removal of blame from him in cases of insanity until he recovers, sleep until he wakes, forgetfulness until he remembers, and cases of coercion, and the increase of his responsibility with the increase of his intellectual, physical, and psychological characteristics and capabilities.
Source pages p. 225

Commentary
This passage defines the method of concomitant variation (طريقة التغير النسبي) as one of the methods for establishing causal relationships. The author begins with an analogy: a set of keys controlling different functions, where we want to identify the fuel key. By observing that turning the assumed key produces proportional changes in ignition (increase, decrease, extinction) while other keys do not, we infer causation. The method requires both the presence of the phenomenon when the cause is present, absence when the cause is absent, and importantly, proportional variation: as the cause quantity increases, the effect quantity increases in parallel, and similarly for decrease. This adds strength beyond the methods of agreement and difference alone. The author then gives a detailed scientific example from Pasteur's germ theory. Pasteur first used the method of difference (with two tubes, one sealed, one open) to show that exposure to air (carrying germs) causes decomposition. Then he applied the method of concomitant variation: he placed groups of tubes in different locations with varying germ concentrations (rural vs. high altitude) and observed that the rate of decomposition varied proportionally with germ presence. Finally, the author applies this to Islamic legal theory: human responsibility is linked to voluntary capacity (kash iradi). Evidence includes: reward/punishment based on intention (niyya), removal of responsibility in insanity, sleep, forgetfulness, and coercion, and increasing responsibility with increasing intellectual, physical, and psychological abilities. This shows proportional variation between capacity and responsibility, confirming the causal link.

Key Terms
طريقة التغير النسبي
السبب
الظاهرة
الكسب الإرادي

Key Takeaway
The method of concomitant variation strengthens causal inference by showing proportional changes, and is applied in both natural sciences and Islamic law.

Induction and Analogy

Methods of Difference and Concomitant Variation
Explains two inductive methods with biological and Islamic legal examples.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the method of difference and the method of concomitant variation to identify causal relationships in Islamic law and theology.

Core Idea
Two inductive methods — difference and concomitant variation — provide rigorous tools for establishing causality.

In this lesson, we explore two powerful inductive methods for identifying causes: the method of difference and the method of concomitant variation. The passage from Prabowo's 'Dawabit al-Ma'rifa' illustrates these methods with a biological experiment by Pasteur and then applies them to Islamic legal theory, showing how human responsibility varies with ability. Understanding these methods will sharpen your ability to analyze causal claims in Fiqh, Usul al-Fiqh, and Kalam.

Guided Path
1
Understand the method of difference
Identify two cases that are identical in all respects except for one factor. If the outcome differs, that factor is the cause. In Pasteur's experiment, two sugar solutions were identical except one was open to air; only the open one rotted, proving airborne organisms cause rot.
This method requires that the two cases be exactly alike except for the one variable.
2
Apply the method of difference to Islamic law
Construct a scenario in Islamic legal reasoning: compare two contracts that are identical except for the presence of interest (riba). The contract with interest is invalid, so interest is the cause of invalidity. This is how jurists identify the 'illah (effective cause).
3
Understand the method of concomitant variation
Observe how changes in a presumed cause correspond proportionally to changes in the effect. In Pasteur's second experiment, the rate of rot varied with the concentration of germs in the air, confirming the causal link.
This method can show both direct and inverse correlations.
4
Apply the method of concomitant variation to Islamic law
Use the passage's example: human responsibility varies with ability (istita'a), intention, and physical/mental capacities. As ability increases, responsibility increases; as it decreases, responsibility decreases. This proportional variation shows that ability is the cause of responsibility.
This method is particularly useful for complex phenomena where perfect control is impossible.

كلتيهما كميتين متساويتين من محلول السكر، وعقمهما في ماء تزيد درجة حرارته على ١٠٠ سنتيجراد، ثم أغلق فوهة إحداهما وترك الأخرى مفتوحة ومعرضة للهواء ووضعهما في ظروف متماثلة تماماً عدا هذين الظرفين. وبعد مدة من الزمن فحص السائلين، فوجد أن المفتوحة منهما هي التي بدأت تتعفن، وأما المغلقة فظلت محافظة على وضعها السليم، فتأكد بطريقة الاختلاف، أن التعفن ناشيء عن حيوانات دقيقة جداً يحملها الهواء فتنتقل إلى المواد القابلة للتعفن، وتتكاثر متغذية بها. ثم تابع تأكده فاستخدم طريقة التغير النسبي، فأخذ ثلاث مجموعات من الأنابيب، عدد كل منها عشرون أنبوبة، ثم ملأها بسائل معين، ثم عقم الأنابيب، وأغلق فوهاتها جميعاً، ثم وضع كل مجموعة في مكان معين، ثم فتحها في أمكنتها. وبعد مدة من الزمن وجد أن نسبة التعفن قد اختلفت باختلاف نسبة الرياح الحاملة للجراثيم، وأن زيادة التعفن كانت ملازمة لزيادة نسبة الجراثيم في الهواء، وذلك حين يكون الهواء أكثر تعرضاً للتلوث بالجراثيم، كمناطق الريف، وأن تناقص التعفن كان ملازماً لتناقص نسبة الجراثيم في الهواء، كالمناطق المرتفعة، والمناطق ذات الجليد الدائم، وهي المناطق التي وزع فيها «باستير» أنابيب التجربة. ومن أمثلة تطبيق هذه الطريقة في الشرعيات موضوع ارتباط مسؤولية الإنسان باستطاعته وبكسبه الإرادي، واعتبار هذا الكسب الإرادي المستطاع هو السبب في المسؤولية. ويستدل للتحقق من هذا السبب، بتقرير محاسبته على مقدار نيته في العمل، بالثواب أو بالعقاب، وبرفع المؤاخذة عنه في حالات الجنون حتى يفيق، والنوم حتى يستيقظ، والنسيان حتى يتذكر، وفي حالات الإكراه، وبمتزايد مسؤوليته بمقدار تزايد خصائصه وقدراته الفكرية والجسدية والنفسية وما يملك من سلطات، وهي التي تمثل وجوه استطاعته، وبتناقص مسؤوليته بمقدار تناقص هذه الأمور لديه، حتى الدرجة الدنيا التي تنعدم معها المسؤولية تماماً. قيمة هذه الطريقة : ظاهر أن هذه الطريقة إذا تيسرت فهي أفضل من كل الطرق السابقة، لأنها تجمع مزاياها، وتزيد عليها دليل التلازم في نسبة التغير طرداً وعكساً، فهي تبين أساس الصلة بين السبب والظاهرة، وتبينها أيضاً من الناحية الكمية، وتكشف ما بينهما من ارتباط دقيق، وتعطي الباحث مجالاً لتسجيل هذا الترابط الكمي والانتفاع منه . وهذه الطريقة نافعة في دراسة الظواهر المعقدة المتشابكة، كالظواهر الاجتماعية، إذ تسمح باكتشاف الأسباب والتحقق منها في ضوء النسب العددية . قالوا : وكانت هذه الطريقة سبباً في معرفة علة المد والجزر، وفي معرفة قانون «بويل» في الغازات، كما أمكن بها تحديد العلاقة بين العرض والطلب في مجال الاقتصاد، إلى غير ذلك من أمور كثيرة لا تحصى .
Both of them are equal quantities of sugar solution, and he sterilized them in water exceeding 100 degrees centigrade, then he closed the mouth of one and left the other open and exposed to the air and placed them in completely identical conditions except for these two circumstances. After a period of time, he examined the two liquids, and found that the open one had begun to rot, while the closed one remained intact, thus confirming by the method of difference that rot originates from very small organisms carried by the air, which transfer to materials susceptible to rot and multiply by feeding on them. Then he continued his verification by using the method of concomitant variation. He took three groups of tubes, each group containing twenty tubes, then filled them with a specific liquid, then sterilized the tubes, and closed all their mouths, then placed each group in a specific location, then opened them in their places. After a period of time, he found that the rate of rot varied with the variation in the proportion of winds carrying germs, and that an increase in rot was concomitant with an increase in the proportion of germs in the air, when the air is more exposed to contamination by germs, such as rural areas, and that a decrease in rot was concomitant with a decrease in the proportion of germs in the air, such as high-altitude areas and areas with permanent ice, which are the areas where Pasteur distributed the experimental tubes. Among examples of applying this method in religious matters is the topic of linking human responsibility to his ability and his voluntary acquisition, and considering this voluntary and possible acquisition as the cause of responsibility. Evidence for verifying this cause is established by determining his accountability according to the amount of his intention in the deed, whether for reward or punishment, and by removing blame from him in cases of insanity until he recovers, sleep until he wakes, forgetfulness until he remembers, and in cases of coercion, and by his responsibility increasing with the increase of his intellectual, physical, and psychological characteristics and abilities and the authorities he possesses, which represent aspects of his ability, and by his responsibility decreasing with the decrease of these matters in him, down to the lowest level where responsibility completely disappears. The value of this method: It is apparent that if this method is feasible, it is better than all previous methods, because it combines their advantages and adds to them the proof of concomitance in the proportion of variation directly and inversely. So it shows the basis of the connection between cause and phenomenon, and also shows it from a quantitative perspective, and reveals the precise correlation between them, and gives the researcher scope to record this quantitative correlation and benefit from it. And this method is useful in studying complex and intertwined phenomena, such as social phenomena, as it allows for discovering causes and verifying them in light of numerical proportions. They said: And this method was the reason for knowing the cause of tides, and for knowing Boyle's law in gases, and it made possible determining the relationship between supply and demand in economics, and many other countless matters.
Source pages p. 226

Commentary
This passage explains two inductive methods for establishing causality: the method of difference and the method of concomitant variation. It begins with a biological experiment by Pasteur to demonstrate the method of difference: two identical sugar solutions are treated identically except one is open to air; only the open one rots, proving that airborne organisms cause rot. Then it describes the method of concomitant variation with another experiment: different groups of tubes placed in various locations show that the rate of rot varies proportionally with germ concentration in the air. This establishes a quantitative correlation. The passage then applies the method of concomitant variation to Islamic legal theory: human responsibility is linked to ability and voluntary acquisition. Evidence includes that accountability varies with intention, and that responsibility increases or decreases with intellectual, physical, and psychological capacities, and vanishes in cases like insanity, sleep, forgetfulness, or coercion. This shows a concomitant relationship between responsibility and ability. The evaluation states that this method is superior because it combines advantages of previous methods and adds proof of proportional concomitance, both direct and inverse. It is useful for complex phenomena like social ones, and historically has been used to discover tides, Boyle's law, and economic relationships.

طريقة التغير النسبي
التلازم

The Method of Residues in Induction
Explains the method of residues for identifying the cause of a remaining part of a phenomenon.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the method of residues to identify the cause of a remaining part of a phenomenon in Islamic legal reasoning.

Core Idea
The method of residues isolates the cause of the unknown part by process of elimination.

The method of residues is a powerful inductive tool for situations where a phenomenon is composed of multiple parts, each with a known or unknown cause. By systematically attributing known causes to known parts, we can infer that the leftover part must be caused by the remaining cause. This method appears in Islamic legal theory when multiple evidences contribute to a ruling, and we need to identify the evidence for an unexplained aspect.

Guided Path
1
Decompose the phenomenon
Break the overall phenomenon into its constituent parts. Each part must be distinct and separately observable. For example, in a legal ruling, identify the individual conditions or components.
2
Attribute known parts to known causes
For each part that has a known cause from prior knowledge, assign that cause. This step relies on already established causal links.
3
Identify the residue
After attributing all known parts, observe the part that remains unexplained. This is the residue that needs a cause.
4
Infer the cause of the residue
Conclude that the residue must be caused by the remaining cause, assuming the total number of causes equals the number of parts and that no other unknown causes are involved.
5
Evaluate the assumption
Consider whether the decomposition is complete and whether the causes are independent. The method's validity depends on these assumptions being met.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
شرح الطريقة الخامسة : وهي النظر في البواقي . تستخدم هذه الطريقة إذا كانت الظاهرة مجزأة إلى عدة أجزاء، وكانت لهذه الأجزاء أسباب بعددها، وعرف الباحث علاقة بعض أجزاء الظاهرة بأسبابها، فإذا علق كل جزء بسببه المعروف لديه، ولم يبق أخيراً إلا جزء واحد، فإنه يستطيع أن يعلقه بالسبب الباقي، فيكون الجزء الباقي من الظاهرة معللاً بالفرد الباقي من الأسباب . نظير ما لو كان لدينا ثلاثة أزواج من الأسلاك الكهربائية ولها ثلاثة مفاتيح، فإذا عرفنا مفتاح الزوج الأول منها، ثم عرفنا مفتاح الزوج الثاني منها، وضح لنا بالبداهة أن الزوج الثالث هو للمفتاح الثالث .
Explanation of the fifth method: it is the consideration of residues. This method is used if the phenomenon is divided into several parts, and these parts have causes equal to their number, and the researcher knows the relationship of some parts of the phenomenon to their causes. Then, if he attributes each part to its known cause, and in the end there remains only one part, he can attribute it to the remaining cause. So the remaining part of the phenomenon is explained by the remaining individual of the causes. An analogy: if we have three pairs of electrical wires and they have three switches, and we know the switch of the first pair, then we know the switch of the second pair, it becomes obvious that the third pair belongs to the third switch.
Source pages p. 227

Commentary
This passage explains the method of residues (tariqat al-bawaqi). It is used when a phenomenon can be broken down into parts, each with a known cause. After accounting for the known cause-effect pairs, the remaining part of the phenomenon must be caused by the remaining cause. The text provides an analogy: three pairs of electrical wires with three switches. If we know which switch controls the first pair and which controls the second, the remaining pair is necessarily controlled by the remaining switch. This method is useful in complex investigations where multiple causal factors are at play. In Islamic jurisprudence, for example, if a hadith text has multiple chains and we identify the narrators for some parts, the remaining part is attributed to the remaining narrator.

Key Terms
النظر في البواقي

Key Takeaway

The Method of Residues: Logic and Definition
Defining the method of residues with its structural logic.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the logic of the method of residues and correctly apply it to a simple phenomenon.

Core Idea
Subtract known causes; the leftover cause explains the leftover effect.

The method of residues (النظر في البواقي) is a canonical inductive technique that isolates a cause by elimination. The author introduces it as a natural process of human reasoning, illustrated with an electrical analogy and formalized by Stuart Mill. This lesson breaks down its logical steps and common pitfalls.

Guided Path
1
Identify the total phenomenon
What is the complex event or set of occurrences you are analyzing? This is the broad subject that can be broken into parts.
In the examples: several crimes, a revolution.
2
Decompose the phenomenon into distinct parts
Each part must be separable and correspond to a specific cause. The parts should collectively cover the whole phenomenon.
Each crime is a part; each group of revolutionaries is a part.
3
Match known causes to their parts
For some parts, we already know the cause (e.g., criminals confessed to specific crimes; revolutionaries were ambitious or hired). Link these causes to their effects.
This step requires prior knowledge of causal relationships.
4
Attribute the remainder to the remaining cause
The part with no known cause must be caused by the remaining cause. This is the core inference of the method.
The unconfessed crime belongs to the unconfessing criminal; the remaining revolutionaries are motivated by resentment.
5
Verify the exclusivity condition
The method only works if the parts and causes are mutually exclusive and collectively exhaustive. Overlap or hidden causes undermine the conclusion.
In the revolution example, if some participants had both ambition and resentment, the residual cause is not uniquely identified.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
شرح الطريقة الخامسة : وهي النظر في البواقي . تستخدم هذه الطريقة إذا كانت الظاهرة مجزأة إلى عدة أجزاء، وكانت لهذه الأجزاء أسباب بعددها، وعرف الباحث علاقة بعض أجزاء الظاهرة بأسبابها، فإذا علق كل جزء بسببه المعروف لديه، ولم يبق أخيراً إلا جزء واحد، فإنه يستطيع أن يعلقه بالسبب الباقي، فيكون الجزء الباقي من الظاهرة معللاً بالفرد الباقي من الأسباب . نظير ما لو كان لدينا ثلاثة أزواج من الأسلاك الكهربائية ولها ثلاثة مفاتيح، فإذا عرفنا مفتاح الزوج الأول منها، ثم عرفنا مفتاح الزوج الثاني منها، وضح لنا بالبداهة أن الزوج الثالث هو للمفتاح الثالث . وطريقة الطرح بربط المعلوم بالمعلوم، وحصر الباقي بالباقي، طريق مستخدمة في الفكر اليومي عند الإنسان، لذلك نجد النصوص البليغة كثيراً ما تترك بيان ربط البواقي من الأسباب بمسبباتها، اعتماداً على فهم الفكر له من غير جهد، وإيجازاً في الكلام. وقد عرّف «ستيوارت ميل» هذه الطريقة بقوله: «اطرح من أي ظاهرة الأشياء المعروف أنها معلولة لبعض علل معروفة فيكون الباقي من الظاهرة معلولاً للبعض الآخر من تلك العلل». أمثلة على تطبيق هذه الطريقة: ١ - ظهرت عدة جرائم، وقُبض المجرمون، واعترفوا إلا واحداً منهم لم يعترف بجريمته، فإننا سنحكم بأنه صاحب الجريمة الباقية، سواء اعترف أو لم يعترف، لأن العلم بكونه مجرماً متحقق لدينا، والذي نبحث عنه إنما هو تعيين الجريمة التي ارتكبها هو. ٢ - قامت ثورة على السلطة الحاكمة في بلد ما، فعلمنا أن بعض المشتركين فيها طامعون بالحكم، وأن بعض المشتركين مستأجرون بالمال، وعلمنا أن النقمة على سياسة السلطة الحاكمة من أسباب الثورة، عندئذ نعلم - عن طريق حصر البواقي - أن الثائرين الذين ليسوا طامعين بالحكم ولا مستأجرين بالمال، هم ناقمون على سياسة السلطة الحاكمة. ٣ - ومن أمثلة استخدام هذه الطريقة في الشرعيات ما يلي:
Explanation of the fifth method: which is consideration of the residues. This method is used when the phenomenon is divided into several parts, and these parts have causes equal to their number, and the researcher knows the relationship of some parts of the phenomenon to their causes. So if he links each part to its known cause, and finally only one part remains, then he can link it to the remaining cause, so the remaining part of the phenomenon is caused by the remaining individual of the causes. An analogy: if we have three pairs of electrical wires and they have three switches, and we know the switch of the first pair, then we know the switch of the second pair, it becomes evident to us that the third pair corresponds to the third switch. And the method of subtraction by linking the known to the known, and confining the remaining to the remaining, is a method used in everyday human thought. Therefore, we find that eloquent texts often leave out the explanation of linking the remaining causes to their effects, relying on the mind's understanding of it without effort, and for brevity in speech. Stuart Mill defined this method by saying: 'Subtract from any phenomenon those parts that are known to be caused by certain known causes, then the remainder of the phenomenon is caused by the other parts of those causes.' Examples of applying this method: 1 - Several crimes appeared, the criminals were arrested, and they confessed except for one of them who did not confess to his crime. Then we will judge that he is the perpetrator of the remaining crime, whether he confesses or not, because the knowledge that he is a criminal is established for us, and what we are searching for is only the identification of the crime he committed. 2 - A revolution occurred against the ruling authority in a country. We knew that some of the participants were ambitious for power, and some participants were hired for money, and we knew that resentment against the policy of the ruling authority is among the causes of the revolution. Then we know - by means of confining the residues - that the revolutionaries who are neither ambitious for power nor hired for money are resentful against the policy of the ruling authority. 3 - And among the examples of using this method in religious matters are the following:
Source pages p. 227

Commentary
This passage defines the method of residues (النظر في البواقي), one of the inductive methods for establishing causation. The author explains that when a phenomenon can be broken into parts, and each part except one has a known cause, the remaining part must be caused by the remaining cause. An electrical analogy illustrates the logic: if two switches are linked to two wire pairs, the third pair must correspond to the third switch by elimination. The author emphasizes that this method is intuitive and used in everyday reasoning, and cites Stuart Mill's formal definition. Three examples follow: a criminal case where the unconfessed crime is attributed to the only unconfessing criminal; a revolution where participants' motives are deduced by eliminating known motives (ambition and bribery), leaving resentment; and a reference to applications in religious rulings (الشرعيات). The passage does not complete the third example but sets up its use in Islamic jurisprudence, where the method can be applied, for instance, to determine the effective cause (عِلَّة) of a legal ruling by eliminating known possibilities.

Key Terms
النظر في البواقي
الظاهرة
السبب

Key Takeaway
The method of residues attributes the unexplained remainder of a phenomenon to the remainder of its possible causes, but only as a strong inference, not a logical deduction.
